Current Commentary

The Noisy and Prominent Issue of European War Debts

Several years ago, what caused a stir in Europe and shook the United States and Britain was the issue of reparations. However, in recent years, international attention has shifted and focused on the war debt issue. The so-called war debt issue refers to the situation during the previous World War when the Allied Powers needed military supplies and relied on the United States as their external treasury. Due to a lack of cash, the supply of military supplies was transformed into loans, which are the so-called war debts. Since the conclusion of the Treaty of Versailles, defeated Germany has had to pay more than 20 billion gold marks in reparations annually. The income from the people's sweat and blood is provided to the government, which in turn pays it to the Allied Powers. The European Allied Powers must further provide a large part of their reparations income to the United States to pay for the principal and interest on war debts. The reason why the United States has become the world's largest creditor nation, and why New York has replaced London as the world's financial center, and why the power of American international financial capitalism has spread throughout the globe, is all thanks to the World War.

Any precise and reliable theory, golden rule, or regulation must have substantial economic conditions as its safeguard. Once times change, even if the speaker is eloquent, it will ultimately be impossible to overcome the changed reality. The reason why there was once a fierce debate over reparations, and today it is limited to the simple issue of war debts, is precisely because of this. After more than ten years of collecting reparations, Germany's finances have reached the point of exhaustion. However, after more than ten years of recuperation, Germany's national strength has gradually become unassailable. The Germans, therefore, calmly and unhurriedly informed the world that they were unable to pay reparations. If the European Allied Powers were to use force against Germany, it would only push Germany towards extremism. A single spark would ignite the whole plain, and quickly lead all of Europe to communism. Moreover, the internal suspicions and conflicts of the so-called European Allied Powers are becoming increasingly acute. Since Britain and Italy both want to support Germany to resist France, the so-called force is likely to only make France the target of public criticism.

Since the continued payment of reparations is not permitted by reality, the only option is to shift the focus to war debts. In this regard, US President Hoover adopted a strategy of seizing the initiative. Before the European nations issued communiqués requesting a postponement of war debt payments, he generously and voluntarily announced last winter a one-year moratorium on war debt payments. At that time, the whole world praised him, and the Soviet Union was shocked, considering it an unexpected move in the conflict of imperialism. Hoover's initial hope was also to use this to quickly revive the world from panic and restore prosperity, so that the life of capitalism could be extended indefinitely, and the payment of war debts would no longer be a problem. However, in the blink of an eye, the one-year period has expired, and the world's panic is still ongoing. The war debt issue has once again become a noisy and prominent issue. This is something that Hoover did not anticipate at the outset.

Speaking of the war debt issue, the most intense disputes between Europe and the United States involve two points. One is the linked relationship between war debts and reparations. The European Allied Powers believe that the payment of war debts should be conditional on the receipt of reparations. Therefore, if Germany is unable to continue paying reparations, the Allied Powers will also stop paying war debts. The United States has always maintained that reparations are one matter, and war debts are another matter, and that a public linked relationship between them should not be allowed. Recently, Britain has also stated that the receipt of war debt payments from France is a condition for the payment of all British war debts to the United States. This is because, during the war, the United States believed that Britain had stronger international credit and lent money to the Allied Powers mainly through Britain, which then re-lent it to other Allied Powers. Since there was already a linked relationship in fact during the lending, Britain is now proposing a linked relationship in return to counter the US position. Therefore, in addition to the linked relationship between war debts and reparations, there is also a linked relationship between war debts and war debts. The complexity of the situation is such that onlookers feel lost in a fog.

The second point of contention between Europe and the United States is the issue of individual resolution versus overall resolution. The Lausanne Conference is where the European powers united to deal with the American war debt issue. The United States is unwilling to see the European nations establish a united front, and also believes that this kind of united front is detrimental to negotiations. Therefore, it has repeatedly stated that it is willing to negotiate the war debt issue separately with any European Allied Power, but is unwilling to negotiate with any international group. In addition, it has sent important political and financial figures to lobby European countries in an attempt to break their united front. Observing the state of their mutual suspicion and rivalry, it is evident that the conflicts between the great powers can never be expected to be resolved.

However, can the united front among the European powers be maintained without being broken? From Britain's perspective, the huge sum of 30 million pounds is indeed a pity to spend. However, it ultimately does not want to see the once-incomparable British Empire become someone unable to repay debts. Therefore, it has to use the linked relationship of its claims on France as the reason for its inability to fully repay. The French, however, see this as a means for the British to shift the blame to France. The discord between Britain and France has already opened up the possibility of a rupture in the united front.

Based on our current observations, Britain and France will likely pay the war debts due this time after all, but with the condition that the war debts must be reorganized. At the international economic conference to be held next year, the United States may allow a reduction in war debts on the condition of disarmament. However, from the Hague Reparation Conference in 1930 to the suspension of war debts in 1931, the deterioration of the world situation is becoming more and more serious. Even if the war debt issue can be temporarily resolved, it is only a manifestation of temporarily patching up the situation.

There is News of a Connection Between the Yuehan and Guangjiu Railways

(Nanjing) According to reports from the Ministry of Railways, the Guangdong provincial government has borrowed 15 million yuan from Hong Kong as an exchange condition for connecting the Yuehan and Guangjiu railways. The government has not yet received a formal report on this matter. However, if the connection between the two railways becomes a reality, it will be greatly detrimental to us. The Yuehan Railway is connected to the Pinghan Railway, and is a trunk line that runs vertically through our country from north to south. In the future, once the Shaozhu section is completed, the north-south transportation will be convenient, and goods can be transported by land. At that time, maritime transportation will be hit. In other words, Hong Kong's business will be taken away by Guangzhou in part. However, if the Yuehan Railway is connected to the Guangjiu Railway, the situation will be very different. After the connection, not only can goods from the north be directly transported to Kowloon for export without having to be shipped from Guangzhou, Guangzhou's business will gradually decline. At the same time, the economic power of the British in Hong Kong can penetrate deep into the interior. In the future, foreign goods will have to gather in Hong Kong. Thus, the construction of ports and Zhongshan port in our country's plan, even if successful, will lose its function. (2nd Day Special Dispatch)

After the British Note Arrived in Washington, the White House Held Discussions All Night

A Statement Will Be Issued Again to Declare the Position of the United States

The Attitude Towards War Debts is Not Completely Without Room for Change

National News Agency, Washington, 1st Telegram: The British war debt note was delivered to the US State Department by the British Embassy this morning. The full text is over 5,000 words long. Secretary of State Stimson, upon receiving it, immediately went to the White House to discuss the matter with the President. It is expected that after the full text is published, another statement will be issued to announce the US government's position. It is noted that President-elect Roosevelt will not be consulted this time, as Mr. Roosevelt once declared that the payment due on December 15th is "not his baby." Therefore, the government is respecting his words and will not send a copy of the British note in advance. The content will be notified to Mr. Roosevelt when it is published. As for the publication date, according to Deputy Secretary of State Castle, it will be around Friday. Currently, political and financial figures believe that Stimson's previous rejection of the suspension of payment note is not the final word of the US government on this issue, and there is absolutely no room for change.

National News Agency, Washington, 1st Telegram: Although US congressmen still declare that the people do not approve of the suspension of foreign debts, the US President, after receiving the British note, is quite hesitant. Although congressmen have received telegrams from various constituencies opposing concessions to debtor countries, prominent economists across the country have also telegraphed the government. However, the content has not been released. It is only known that the President, Secretary of State Stimson, and Secretary of the Treasury Mills considered and reviewed the matter late into the night. According to reports, after receiving the British note today, Stimson rushed to the White House to meet with the President. Later, he summoned Secretary of the Treasury Mills to the palace. The three held discussions for more than an hour. Although the details of the meeting were not released afterward, sources close to the government say that the British note strongly argued that if the United States insists on payment in mid-December, it will seriously damage world commerce. This has deeply impressed US government officials. In addition, many sources here say that the wording of the British note is extremely frank and complete.

The Eloquent British Note

Reuters, London, 1st Telegram: The British note to the United States was sent out today. The note details the reasons why Britain believes that war debts and reparations are exacerbating the world's decline. It states that war debts and reparations are one of the main causes of the world's decline. The total amount of debts borrowed in the form of goods rather than money is as follows: The United States lent 2,055,000,000 yuan to the Allied countries, Britain lent 1,600,000,000 yuan to European Allied countries, and France lent 460,000,000 yuan to other Allied countries. The possibility of paying reparations and war debts temporarily exists only when investment funds flow from the United States to Europe. However, once an economic crisis breaks out, creditors withdraw their funds, and panic spreads. The credit on which private investment relies is destroyed by repeated shocks, and currency prices are unstable, and collapse is a concern. Although restrictions are imposed, they only increase disputes. If the causes of the disruption, such as intergovernmental debts, are not addressed, the world cannot even consider how to restore financial institutions. In the final analysis, international debts can only be repaid with goods. A 1925 US Treasury Department report established a principle that debtor countries must be allowed to place their finances and monetary systems on a stable basis. Today, the continued payment of war debts is completely contrary to this principle. Creditor countries only receive tens of millions of dollars, but this prolongs the world's turmoil, which is also of no benefit to creditor countries. It is the right of all governments in the world, especially the US and British governments, to work together on the first necessary step to prevent financial, economic, and political disasters. The United States lent 2,055,000,000 yuan, and Britain lent 1,600,000,000 yuan. For the benefit of taxpayers, the United States has recovered 434,000,000 yuan, while Britain has received nothing. Britain's debt to the United States accounts for 40% of the debt released by the United States, and Britain's payment to the United States accounts for 80% of the debt recovered by the United States. Moreover, what is given is actually the price of goods, and the price of goods paid today is double the price at the time of borrowing. Since the United States raised tariffs, British goods have been greatly affected. Britain has always been the best consumer of American goods, but if war debts continue to be paid, it will limit the British people's purchasing power of American goods. Furthermore, in terms of the Lausanne settlement, Britain has given up the debts owed by others while continuing to pay its own debts. This is absolutely unacceptable. Britain's foreign exchange reserves are currently insufficient to meet the December debt. The only other way is to pay the debt with gold bars, which would greatly sacrifice the Bank of England's gold reserves. The Bank of England's current holdings are only sufficient to meet its obligations as a financial center in London. The British government firmly believes that delaying the December debt payment will definitely promote world prosperity and recovery. Therefore, it asks the United States to discuss how to delay the payment. The Lausanne settlement, which was established based on President Hoover's temporary suspension of payments, has established a foundation of trust and security. If the war debt issue is reopened now, it will cause panic again. The above is the general idea of the British note to the United States, which aims to reopen the door for satisfactory discussions. The wording is extremely cautious to avoid provocative tones and presents reasons and figures to show that it does not want American taxpayers to bear an even greater sacrifice than British taxpayers. The purpose of this note is also to correct the misconception that canceling war debts would financially benefit Britain.

Japan Plans to Attack the Righteous Army with Four Divisions

The Righteous Army Has Retreated Into the Deep Mountains Awaiting Next Spring to Launch a Campaign; The Puppet State Issues Paper Currency to Manipulate the Finances of the Northeast

A Tianjin dispatch reports that a certain gentleman recently returned from an inspection tour outside the Great Wall and has obtained very detailed information. A summary is provided below:

Throughout the railways outside the Great Wall, both at large and small stations, there are stationed soldiers. Japanese soldiers treat the Northeast as conquered territory and the Chinese people as enslaved subjects of a vanquished nation. Their actions are extremely tyrannical. Coupled with a group of shameless Chinese traitors, who are heartlessly rebellious, acting as accomplices, they have made it difficult for the people in various places to live in peace, and they live in constant fear of death. Wealthy families are often accused of colluding with bandits, so their family property can be confiscated. Patriotic individuals, unwilling to accept their subjugation, have united with armed comrades to resist Japan and punish traitors. These righteous armies resisting Japan and punishing traitors were very powerful in the spring and summer of this year. The total number cannot be statistically determined, but it is estimated to be over one million. However, without leadership, their strength is somewhat scattered. Moreover, due to a lack of ammunition supplies, it is difficult for them to sustain themselves. From autumn to winter, the weather becomes colder day by day. It has now reached below ten degrees Celsius, making it impossible to operate near the railway lines. The National Salvation Army in various parts of southern Liaoning has retreated into the deep mountains to preserve their strength and await an opportunity to act.

The Japanese method of eliminating the righteous army initially involved bombing with aircraft. Whenever villages or county towns were found to harbor the righteous army, they would be bombed until they were turned into scorched earth. Next, they prohibited civilians from stockpiling grain in order to cut off the righteous army's supplies. However, this method did not work and only caused local devastation, increasing the people's determination to resist Japan. The Japanese then changed their strategy, conducting household registration and confiscating civilian self-defense firearms. Little did they know that people regarded firearms as their lives, so the result was only increased resentment. Seeing that their plan was unsuccessful, the Japanese changed their plans again, engaging in pacification efforts. They dispatched more than ten pacification officers, including Oyatsuki Yuushin (Advisor to the Kwantung Army Headquarters and concurrently Advisor to the First Cavalry Brigade of the Jilin Garrison), Ato Koichi (Attached to the Jilin Railway Guard Command and concurrently Military Instructor), and Kihara Kunisuke (of the Japanese Kwantung State Fisheries and Aquaculture Joint Venture). Each carried large sums of money, spreading rumors everywhere, using generous bribes and promises of high official positions to lure the weaker elements of the righteous army. Some of these smaller righteous army groups, feeling that their situation was difficult, were indeed deceived. However, after the Japanese pacified them, they immediately sent personnel to inspect them, first paying wages, then confiscating weapons, and finally disbanding them, giving them free train tickets to return home. However, righteous armies with more than three to five thousand men would rather resist Japan and punish traitors until not a single piece of armor remained than surrender. The consuls of Britain, France, and the United States stationed in Changchun, Jilin, protested to the Japanese Kwantung Army Headquarters last month, stating that the Japanese and Manchukuo troops could not maintain law and order, and foreign nationals were constantly in danger. They requested that personnel be sent immediately to protect foreign nationals as they left the country. Japan was deeply disturbed by this protest and immediately sent personnel to express their apologies to the consuls of Britain, the United States, and France, falsely claiming that they would resolve the righteous army issue within three months, hoping that foreign nationals would not leave for the time being. However, the consuls of the various countries believed that the Japanese army was incapable of maintaining security in the three northeastern provinces, so their nationals continued to leave the country en masse. The Japanese army, feeling slighted by the various countries, took it as a disgrace and decided to have Lieutenant General Shaochuan, the general commander of the puppet state, take responsibility for resolving the righteous army issue within four weeks. They also transferred two standing army divisions from Korea and conscripted Koreans to form two more divisions, totaling approximately 70,000 men. They ordered the puppet state's finance department to allocate ten million yuan in puppet paper currency as military expenses. Mobilization has already begun. The first step focuses on the Jilin-Hunchun, Jilin-Changchun, and Jilin-Dunhua routes. The second step focuses on the Mengjiang area. The third step focuses on the armies of Su Bingwen and others in northern Manchuria.

The traitor Zhang HaiPeng has successively recruited bandits, now numbering 144,000, all cavalry. They are stationed in places such as Changchun, Jilin. Their military discipline is very poor, and even the Japanese soldiers are afraid of them. Zhang avoids contact with the righteous army, and many of his subordinates have tacit agreements with the righteous army. Zhang recently wants to drive out Xi Qia and replace him. The Japanese side knows that Zhang has great ambitions and fears future troubles. Therefore, during this large-scale offensive against the righteous army, they dispatched Zhang's troops to take the front lines. Japanese soldiers monitored the rear with machine guns and artillery, and also bombed with aircraft and charged with tanks, intending to make Zhang unable to advance or retreat, until he died. The righteous army, with inferior firearms and insufficient ammunition, could only retreat into the mountains to preserve their strength in the face of this large-scale oppression, and wait for the spring and summer of next year to seek further progress. However, northern Manchuria is extremely cold, currently at twenty or thirty degrees below zero. The hands and feet of Japanese soldiers operating in this climate have already become frostbitten. The Soviet army has been stationed in northern Manchuria for a long time and has adapted to the climate, not feeling the cold. Therefore, since the Soviet army began resisting Japan, the Japanese have suffered no less than 20,000 casualties, while the Soviet army has suffered few casualties. Therefore, it is impossible for the Japanese army to dream of eliminating the Soviet army this winter; it will only result in further sacrifices. As for the puppet state's paper currency policy, since the establishment of the puppet Central Bank, it has issued paper currency in denominations of one yuan, five yuan, and ten yuan. The patterns are similar to those of the Bank of Communications paper currency. The issuance is not fixed, and it is not redeemable, but its credibility is being promoted vigorously. For railways, postal services, telegraphs, taxes, etc., the puppet currency is the primary currency, and other paper currencies and silver dollars are refused. For Fengtian silver dollar notes, Fengtian small silver dollar notes, and Jilin-Heilongjiang official notes, this puppet currency is used to absorb and destroy them. Fortunately, the paper currency of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications is still in normal use because of the public's deep trust, but its value is lower than that of the puppet currency. In addition, the righteous army of Tang Juwu occupies 18 counties in Liaodong and issues military scrip, amounting to several million yuan. Last month, Tang's army was pressured by the Japanese army and retreated to the Mengjiang area. The puppet state still allows the use of this military scrip, but it is only used to exchange it for puppet currency to be burned. Regarding education, the puppet state has established a textbook compilation committee. Currently, schools use textbooks published by the Commercial Press and the Zhonghua Book Company before 1917. Those with anti-Japanese sentiments are stamped with a red "This lesson is invalid" stamp. Primary and secondary schools add a reading of the classics, lecturing on The Doctrine of the Mean, Mencius, The Classic of Filial Piety, The Analects, and Japanese language. In fact, most of the schools in the three eastern provinces, except for those along the railway lines, have been suspended in the counties and towns. (November 30)

Investigation of the Salt Industry in Guangdong and Qiongzhou

Salt production in various ports still uses old methods

Annual production is about several million yuan

A Guangzhou dispatch reports that Qiongya Island in Guangdong Province is surrounded by the sea on all four sides. In addition to the abundant but undeveloped forests and mineral resources on the island, the fishing industry is also a major source of profit. Unfortunately, fishing does not employ new methods, and there is no large-scale company to operate it, so the fishing industry is not developed. Moreover, fishing rights have recently fallen into the hands of foreigners. Only the local salt industry can maintain its former profits because of its proximity to the sea, accounting for a large proportion of local products. However, salt producers have not been able to use scientific methods to improve production, which is regrettable. The Construction Department recently sent an investigation team to conduct on-site investigations to develop industries in Qiongya. Details of the current situation of the Qiongya salt industry are as follows: (1) Sanya Port Salt Industry: The Sanya salt fields cover a total of 2,441 acres, with a construction cost of 500 to 800 yuan per acre. The Sanya salt production business was founded in the Dingchou year of the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty (58 years ago). High-quality salt fields produce 300 dan (100 jin per dan) of salt per acre per year, medium-quality salt fields produce 250 to 280 dan, and low-quality salt fields produce 180 to 250 dan. Sanya Port, combined with Yulin Port, can produce approximately 4 million packages of salt per year, worth approximately 2 million yuan. There are 69 salt production stores. (2) Lingao Xinying Port Salt Industry: The salt fields are all made of stone, square or rectangular, and are used exclusively for sun-drying salt. These salt fields are mostly built by private individuals and are not large in scale. The salt produced is fine-grained and of good quality, but production is low. Salt is the main product of Lingao County, with an annual output of approximately 70,000 dan, worth 280,000 yuan. The Wanglong salt field is operated by locals, and the salt produced is transported to Haikou for sale. (3) There are many salt fields in Beili Port, with an annual output of approximately 200,000 dan. Large salt fields can produce more than 10,000 dan of salt per year, medium-sized ones can produce 6,000 to 7,000 dan, and small ones can produce more than 6,000 dan. However, the salt produced is coarse-grained and slightly bitter. The production method is still the same as the natural sun-drying method of the past, with no improvements. The salt fields are divided into two types: one is a dry salt field, used to evaporate water so that the brine crystallizes into salt; the other is a brine storage pond, where brine is stored in the pond, and then waterwheels are used to introduce the water into the dry salt fields for the water to evaporate and become salt. (4) Xinying Port: The annual salt production is also quite large. Building a 9-square-zhang salt field in this area costs approximately 100 yuan. A 300-square-zhang salt field requires seven to ten salt workers. Salt workers earn approximately seven yuan per month. A 200-square-zhang salt field can produce approximately 2,000 dan of salt per year. (November 28)

Niu Lan Is on Hunger Strike Again Because His Request to Be Transferred to a Suzhou Prison Has Been Ignored

The Ta Mei Evening News reports that Niu Lan has petitioned the judicial authorities to allow him and his wife to be transferred from the Jiangsu First Prison in Nanjing to a prison in Suzhou so that their four-year-old child can visit them more conveniently from Shanghai. However, the authorities ignored his request, so he has resumed his hunger strike, which is now in its seventh day. Niu Lan's wife has not yet gone on hunger strike, but she plans to join him if Niu Lan's request is not approved within a few days.

Joint Defense and Pacification in Various Districts of Guangdong Province

Guangzhou City Military and Police Jointly Conduct Winter Defense

Nine Joint Defense Zones Recently Established in Eastern Guangdong

A Guangzhou dispatch reports that the winter defense season has arrived. The defense forces in various parts of Guangdong Province are successively carrying out winter defense. In the urban area of Guangzhou, the military police and the armed security team of the Provincial Public Security Bureau jointly protect the defense affairs inside and outside the city. In addition to sending detachments to garrison in the suburbs, the security team has also organized patrol teams to shuttle back and forth day and night. The military police have also recently formed a bicycle patrol team to carry out patrol duties, inspecting the travel documents of the public and the gun licenses at night to guard against criminals. Military and political organs have also implemented ordinary martial law, so the security situation is still relatively peaceful. In addition, joint defense has been established successively in the east, west, north. In northern Guangdong, a joint military police patrol office has been established in Nanxiong and Shaozhou to ban prostitution at night to prevent criminals from mixing in. In western Guangdong, the three counties of Gaoyao, Gaoming, and Heshan have formed a joint defense team to actively carry out rural cleaning. Zhaoqing and Yangjiang, Luoding counties organized ZhaoYangLuo Six Prefectures Joint Defence Meeting, headed by defense commander Liu Qishi recently dispatch teams to eradicate local bandits near Emerging area. As for Qiongya in southern Guangdong, which is located on the frontier, the stationed army Chen brigade is currently engaged in suppression of Wang Wenyu band of communist bandits. However, the area is vast, and there is deep concern that there will be no responsible authority to preside over the suppression of bandits if the pacification zone is abolished in the future. Qiongya may be changed to a military administration area, with the current defense commander serving as the director of the area, in order to preside over the suppression of bandits and pacification. As for eastern Guangdong, after the Third Army Commander Li Yangjing planned the bandit suppression measures, he recently divided the eastern districts into nine joint defense zones. Each zone established a joint defense committee, with the county magistrates of each zone serving as members and the commanders of the garrisoned troops in each zone serving as chairmen. They have been established in order. The nine joint defense zones are: (1) the Hailufeng, Zijin, Huiyang District, with Zhang Da, the Director of Pacification of ten counties in Huizhou, concurrently serving as the chairman of the Joint Defense Committee; (2) the Huizhou, Boluo, Zijin District, with Li Zhenliang as the chairman of the Joint Defense Committee; (3) the Dongguan, Zengcheng, Baoan District, with Zhang Wei as the chairman of the Joint Defense Committee; (4) the Chaozhou, Meizhou, Puning, Hailai District, with Zhang Ruigui as the chairman; (5) the Wuhua, Fengshun District, with Wu Junsheng as the chairman; (6) the Dapu, Raoping, Chaozhou, Meizhou District, with Huang Yanzhen as the chairman; (7) the Jiaoling, Pingyuan District, with Huang Renhuan as the chairman; (8) the Xingning, Longchuan District, with Huang Zhiwen as the chairman; (9) the Heyuan, Lianping, Heping District, with Ouyang Xin as the chairman. (November 25)

Liang Brigade of Liu Zhennian's Troops Arrives in Wenzhou

A Wenzhou dispatch reports that Liu Zhennian's troops of the 21st Division of the Army, having received orders to relocate from Shandong to eastern Zhejiang, Liang Lizhu's brigade of Liu's troops, traveling on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Feng, Tong Hua, and Tai Shun, arrived in Wenzhou at approximately 6:00 AM on the 27th. When the ship arrived at the port, He Lingxiao, the commander of the 4th Regiment of the Wenzhou Security Team, representing the Zhejiang Provincial Government, led a company of soldiers, and Zhang Weichen, the magistrate of Yongjia County, etc., were all at the port to welcome them. The brigade totals approximately 7,000 men, with sufficient supplies and equipment, including more than ten mortars and more than one hundred mules and horses. The Tragic Life of the Border People in Yunnan

A special dispatch from Kunming reports that the border area of Yunnan can be divided into five districts based on administrative divisions and nine districts based on chieftain territories. It borders British Burma and forms a continuous plain with completely identical climate and soil. Since the British have been operating Burma, the border people have relied on the British for everything except livestock and grain. The British used their financial power to monopolize everything concerning the border people. British goods were sold easily, silver coins were manipulated, and labor was exploited. The essence and marrow of the border people flowed westward.

Chieftain heads exploit heavily. What causes the border people to directly feel the annoyance and high pressure of the suffering are none other than the Chieftain. The Chieftain system was established 500 years ago in Ming dynasty under the reigns of those generals such as Fu Youde, Mu Ying, Lan Yu, and Wang Ji who had made great achievements in pacifying the border regions. Those generals where awarded land to rule, enjoyed special privileges, hereditary tenure, with the people hereditary bound to their land. The Chieftains never stop exploitation towards the border residents, with endless exactions and desires. Farming and taxation are commonplace, but the Chief's family, the expenses for any large or small affair, are to be borne by the people. The following fourteen items are what is known, (1) rearing and raising fees when the Chief's offspring are born. (2) marriage fees when the Chief's offspring marry. (3) congratulatory fees upon the Chief's eldest son's succession to office. (4) the cost of repairing the Chief's office and constructing the Chief's residence (5) fees for congratulations during anniversaries and birthdays (6) Medical treatment and burial expenses when the Chief and his wife are sick or die (7) ploughing and harrowing fees when the day for the Establishment of Summer arrives (8) Holiday Fees such as the Dragon Boat Festival and the Mid-Autumn Festival of the lunar calendar, each household is allotted rice, sugar and snacks (9) Frost fees when frost arrives, the Chief prepares banquets. (10) New Year fees in New Years, each household provides meat or its equivalent (11) Fuel Fees, Border regions lack firewood, people dry cattle dung for fuel, but the Chiefs burn fuel provided by the people coming from hundreds of miles away with no compensation (12) Investigation Fees, when the Han officials and the English converge to delimit boundaries, each household are taxed heavily. (13) Carnival Fees, when the Han have festivals, the money used on drinking and plays are extracted from the people, the Chief packages betting and levies duties. (14) Security Fees used to ensure road safety, taxed from merchants. From the summarized items, it is hard to inspect the exact number, but according to merchants that reside there for a while, the fees is at least seven or eight 'kangs' per household every year (each kang being ten robis). For each one dollar a Cheif needs, all levels of leaders will double it, heavy layers of exploitation, the burden is great and the suffering is unspeakable.

Han Officials form a supreme chieftain After the founding of the Republic of China, Li Genyuan began to request the establishment of Han officials when he toured the border regions. Namely today's Five Administrative Districts and the Four Administration Districts, which has far-reaching significance for protecting border areas and consolidating national defense, however, the personnel appointed in the past, most of their only goal is to become officials and get rich. In the places that are like «the sky is high and the emperor is far away», they are able to do as they please, Chieftains need to be subordinates that supplies whatever is requested, so the burden falls on the people, so the border people bear the oppression of the additional "supreme chieftain".

The Budget of the Puppet State – Harbin Correspondence

The so-called "Manchukuo" – everyone knows it is a puppet show stage, even perhaps less than a puppet; purely a tool of Japanese militarists, with no other function. Only strengthening Japan's national defense is close to the truth; even the talk of "lifelines" is just a ghost story to deceive the general Japanese population. Towards the Japanese army, Japanese officials, and Japanese people, they are only docile, perhaps to avoid disaster. Heavy Interest Exploitation, Han Chinese Speculation – Border Residents Trapped in Poverty, Even Drinking Poison to Quench Thirst and Cutting Flesh to Heal Sores, They Are Willing to Do Anything. Han Chinese Seize the Opportunity to Engage in High-Interest Lending to Border Residents. The Known Instances Include: (1) Opium Interest – Every Year After the Frost’s Descent, Han Chinese Enter Barbarian Lands to Sell Coarse Cloth, Needles, and Thread. Poor People Borrow from Them, Borrowing One Ruble, and by the Time the New Opium Enters the Market the Following Spring, in Addition to Repaying the Principal, They Must Add One to Two Ounces of Foreign Opium, Called Opium Interest. There Are Also Those Who Only Pay Interest, Leaving the Principal to Be Paid When the New Opium Enters the Market the Following Year, in Which Case the Opium Interest Is Doubled. If Both Principal and Interest Are Owed, Then the Opium Interest Is Converted to Market Price and Added to the Principal. After Two or Three Years, If the Opium Market Price Rises, There Are Instances Where the Total Owed Is Five to Six Times or Even Seven to Eight Times the Original Principal. (2) Selling Cloth – The Clothing Materials Used by Border Residents Are Generally Supplied by the Three Counties of Tengyue, Baoshan, and Longling. Therefore, in Border Trade, Coarse Cloth Is the Main Commodity, with Needles and Thread Attached. Most Poor People Purchase Cloth on Credit from Han Chinese Each Winter, with the Price Increased by One or Two Tenths, or Even Three or Four Tenths, According to the Market. When the Time Comes and They Have No Money, They Change the Name to "Borrowed," Promising Interest, at a Minimum of Five Percent, or Converting It to New Opium, with Each Bolt of Cloth Exchanged for Five to Six Ounces or Seven to Eight Ounces of Opium. If Measured by the Fair Market Price, The Cloth Price is Invariably Doubled, and the Opium Price Is Only Half. (3) Street Interest – Han Chinese Live in Border Areas and Are Very Familiar with the Border Residents. They Lend Their Savings to Border Residents, One Ruble, with Interest of Ten "Baisa" per Street. With Six Streets per Month, It Totals Sixty "Baisa." Accumulated Over a Year, It Reaches Seven Hundred and Twenty "Baisa." Given that Sixty-Four "Baisa" Can Be Exchanged for One Ruble, This Greatly Exceeds Eleven Times the Principal. Therefore, Han Chinese Who Make a Living by Lending Street Interest in This Area Only Need One Ruble to Support the Average Living of Three to Several Family Members.

Coolie Life, No Different from Cattle and Horses – Border Residents Suffer All Kinds of Aggression from Imperialists Externally, and All Kinds of Oppression from Indigenous Chiefs and Various Headmen Internally. Han Officials Are Only Interested in Profit, and Han Chinese Take the Opportunity to Exploit Them. Buddhist Monks (Including Both Monks and Laypeople) Also Demand Endlessly. The Hardship of the Lives of Border Residents Under These Five Layers of High Pressure Is Self-Evident. Driven by the Pressures of Life, Women Sell Mountain Delicacies, Wild Vegetables, and Fruits, or Weave Cotton and Bamboo Handicrafts. As Soon as Infants Can Leave Their Mothers, They Go to the Wilderness to Tend Pigs and Sheep. Every Year After Autumn, Men Go to Mu-Bang and Burma to Work as Coolies. Those with Some Savings Carry a Load of Sand Pots on a Shoulder Pole, or Carry an Ax and Long Saw, Engaging in the Logging and Sawing of Boards. Those Without Funds Carry the Simplest Luggage, in Groups of Hundreds, Shoulder to Shoulder, Heel to Toe, Called "Poorly Wandering to Barbarian Lands." Once They Enter the Border, They Are Loaded in Carts with Pigs, Horses, Cattle, and Sheep, Driven to Banghai Lao Silver Mine. The Foreman and Stationmaster Hold Whips, Looking Pleased, Treating Them Like Cattle and Horses. At the Slightest Dissatisfaction, They Are Whipped. After Working, Unable to Afford to Return Home, They Risk Going to the Jade and Gem Mines in Mong Kong and Mong Yang in Burmese Territory to Work, Called "Rushing to the Mines." It Is Found That Border Residents Working as Coolies in Barbarian Lands Receive a Monthly Wage of Seventeen Rubles, of Which the Foreman Deducts Two Tenths. Their Work Involves Carrying Minerals and Digging, etc. If the Price of Silver Drops, Wages Are Reduced or Work Is Suspended. Some Die of Starvation and Disease Due to the Interruption of Their Livelihoods. Some Are Imprisoned for Improper Conduct Due to the Pressure of Life. Some Go to Mong Kong and Mong Yang to Obtain Jade and Gems. Therefore, Those Who Return Home Account for Eight or Nine Tenths. As for Working in Jade and Gem Mines, Although the Wages of Workers in the Mines Are Higher Than in Barbarian Lands, Gambling Is Rampant. Border Residents Are Ignorant and Often Get Lost in Gambling, Often Becoming Destitute and Unable to Return Home. The Climate Is Extremely Hot, and Workers Do Not Pay Attention to Hygiene. Deaths Are Everywhere, and Many Are Disabled. Therefore, Those Who Are Fortunate Enough to Return Home Account for Only One or Two Tenths. Border Residents Taste All Kinds of Oppression and Suffering. The So-Called Eighteen Levels of Hell Are Probably Not an Overstatement.

The Difficult Financial Situation in Gansu

Military Spending Accounts for More Than 70% of Total Expenditure

Lanzhou Correspondence. Gansu is located on the frontier, with blocked transportation routes, and therefore its finances are in dire straits. In the past, it received subsidies from other provinces. After the subsidies stopped, it began to maintain itself. In peacetime, the province's revenue could still make do with the current situation. Once an emergency occurred, it would be unable to make ends meet. Since the Great Earthquake of 1920, natural and man-made disasters have followed one after another, resulting in a sharp decline in the province's revenue. The current financial situation of Gansu Province and the reasons for its difficulties are described in detail below.

Tracing back to the Great Earthquake of 1920 as the long-term cause of the financial difficulties in Gansu Province, the disasters of 1928 and 1929 and the conflicts between Hui and Han people were the major causes of its difficulties. In recent years, there has been a military disaster or other major change every few years, resulting in unprecedented poverty. In essence, the long-term cause of Gansu's current predicament should be attributed to natural disasters, and the short-term cause should be attributed to man-made disasters. Setting aside natural disasters for the moment, the man-made disasters are entirely due to the military. The complexity of the military in Gansu Province is far beyond that of other provinces. According to current statistics, there are six divisions, two independent brigades, three guerrilla commanderies, one guard commandery, and so-called cadre school refresher battalions, etc., with at least 95,000 people. With a total population of 6.2 million in Gansu Province, an average of one soldier must be supported for every 65 people. It is estimated that each soldier's salary, supplies, clothing, and military equipment cost at least 150 yuan per year, which means that the burden on the people is an average of 2.3 yuan per person per year. In addition, the horses, excluding the entire cavalry of the First Cavalry Division of Gansu, the horses of other troops, if calculated at 30% of the number of people (the cavalry in the Gansu army are more numerous than those in the armies of the Central Plains provinces), would total more than 33,000 horses. Each horse requires 0.4 yuan per day for supplies, which is 13,200 yuan per day and 4,818,000 yuan per year. Each person must bear another 0.8 yuan. Therefore, military spending alone requires a total burden of 3.1 yuan per person. The total annual military spending for the entire province has exceeded 18 million yuan. Although those in charge have repeatedly reduced it, the various units, in addition to receiving more than 8.65 million yuan from the provincial government, have a shortfall of nearly 10 million, which is entirely taken directly from the peasants, with no room for deficit. The actual amount of grain tax paid by the peasants is only 2.2 million yuan, while the direct cost of supplying the army is four and a half times the grain tax. The reason is that the Gansu army is not only too numerous, but also purely unsystematic, undisciplined, and decentralized. A certain army stationed in a certain place completely regards its defense area as its own sphere of influence, allocating and demanding funds as it pleases. At the slightest dissatisfaction, it tramples on and forces the people to the extreme. People sell their wives and children to fill their desires. For example, this year, out of the 66 counties in the province, more than 50 counties have been affected by drought, hail, insects, frost, and various other natural disasters. The output of rice and grain was originally insufficient. In principle, the price of grain should naturally rise. However, the situation is exactly the opposite. In various counties along Longnan and Longdong, although the grain harvest is poor, the price of grain is not only not high, but is declining daily. Even at a low price, there are no buyers. The reason is that, first, bandits are rampant, and the people are exhausted from running for their lives. Even if they have some food, they cannot store it and cannot carry it with them, so they have no choice but to sell it cheaply. Second, the army forces and extorts them. The people fear their power, and even if there is not enough food, they must endure the pain of selling it to solve their immediate needs. Therefore, the price of grain is extremely low and there is still no market. However, of these two reasons, the latter is even more serious than the former. Banditry is only a temporary phenomenon, while the stationed army is a permanent disaster, leaving the people unable to seek life or death, and spending the year as if in a thicket of thorns. Because the army in Gansu is so complex, none of the province's sources of tax revenue are immune to its destruction. The army intercepts grain taxes in advance in various counties, and directly collecting fines from opium fields has also become a matter of course. It even pre-collects one-third of the taxes for 1933 and 1934. Other departments, such as tobacco, alcohol, and stamps, are all regarded as their own. At the same time, the various armies protect opium and transport goods, which is more than enough to destroy the province's finances. As a result, the provincial treasury has become increasingly empty, the people have become increasingly impoverished, and the reputation of the army has been completely ruined.

Gansu's financial revenue, including national and local taxes, amounts to 13,138,807 yuan per year, while the actual revenue is only 8,802,248 yuan. On the expenditure side, the annual total is 11,180,370 yuan. Military spending alone amounts to 8,652,324 yuan per year, which means that military spending accounts for 77.4% of the total expenditure, or military spending is three and a half times that of all other expenditures. If the actual revenue is compared with military spending, the total actual revenue is only equivalent to military spending.

As for other expenditures, administrative expenses are 892,724 yuan per year, accounting for less than 8% of the total expenditure; party expenses are 100,080 yuan per year, and judicial expenses are 110,112 yuan per year, both accounting for less than 1% of the total expenditure; educational expenses are 584,350 yuan per year, accounting for 5.2% of the total expenditure; administrative expenses for each county are 493,500 yuan per year, accounting for 4.4% of the total expenditure; financial administrative expenses are 240,000 yuan per year, accounting for slightly more than 2% of the total expenditure; and all other expenditures are only more than 99,000 yuan, accounting for less than 1% of the total expenditure. Although there are many troops in Gansu Province, there are still many bandits. According to reports from various counties, there are still more than 6,000 bandits in the province (this is the number compiled from reports from various county governments, and the actual number is probably more than five times this), scattered in various places. Large groups of bandits are not to be discussed, and counties such as Jingyuan, Jingchuan, and Weiyuan each have more than one battalion of troops stationed, but seven or eight bandits can hold machetes and run rampant without hindrance, and are not deterred by the presence of troops. This shows that the soldiers are soldiers and the bandits are bandits.

Implementation Plan for Local Autonomy in Hunan

Ten Designated Counties to Implement Ahead of Schedule

Special Emphasis on Rural Politics

Changsha Correspondence. Because banditry in Hunan Province is gradually spreading, a start was made to promote local autonomy. On the tenth of this month, the Hunan Provincial Local Autonomy Preparatory Committee was formally established. Committee members included: Provincial Government Member Zhai Jianqiu, Huang Shiheng, Wu Jianxue, Provincial Party Committee Member Peng Guojun, Special Autonomy Commissioner Chen Shonong from the Ministry of Interior, Director of the Hunan Provincial Department of Civil Affairs Cao Bowen, Zhou Xueli from the Agricultural Sector, Bin Bucheng from the Labor Sector, Su Jiasheng from the Business Sector, Hu Xinzhi from the Education Sector, Local Gentry Liu Zhaozeng and Wu Zongyu from the Xiangjiang District, Local Gentry Chen Changding and Xiang Yusui from the Wuling District, Local Gentry Liu Chongzhi and Yuan Tongsheng from the Hengyang District, Local Gentry Peng Shidi and Chen Shengjun from the Chenyuan District, and Yu Ruyu, the Section Chief in charge of Autonomy from the Department of Civil Affairs. There were nineteen members in total, and Cao Bowen was designated as Chairman, and Chen Changding as Vice Chairman, to carry out preparations. The Hunan Local Autonomy Implementation Plan has now been formulated and passed at the third regular meeting on the 26th, and sent to the provincial government for promulgation and implementation. The content of the plan is as follows: Chapter 1, Outline. (Article 1) In order to promote local autonomy in this province with a view to realizing it, the province will temporarily designate Changsha, Xiangtan, Hengyang, Hengshan, Shaoyang, Xiangxiang, Yiyang, Changde, Anhua, and Ningxiang as counties for early implementation of autonomy, following the principle of first establishing a scale and then gradually progressing. (Article 2) The administrative guidelines for autonomous counties shall be based entirely on the various autonomy laws and regulations promulgated, with special emphasis on rural politics. (Article 3) The magistrates of autonomous counties shall be appointed in accordance with Article 11 of the Revised County Organization Law, and shall be specially selected from those who have a good reputation, outstanding achievements, and are well-versed in autonomy. (Article 4) At the beginning of the autonomous counties, the magistrates must convene representatives of various agencies, people with a good reputation throughout the county, and leaders of various professional groups to hold a meeting to implement autonomy and innovate county administration, to decide which items of past county administration are not suitable for the urgent needs of the county people, to make appropriate reforms, and to re-formulate the county government's administrative plan based on laws and regulations, and to revise the budget and submit it for approval and implementation. (Article 5) Autonomous counties shall have special commissioners appointed by the provincial government with a good reputation and experience in autonomy studies to work with the county magistrates to train autonomy personnel and promote all autonomy matters. (Article 6) The training matters mentioned in the preceding article shall be formulated by a special commissioner appointed by the provincial government in conjunction with the county magistrate, in accordance with the meaning of Chapters 3 and 4 of the Autonomy Training Institute Regulations and the Autonomy Training Branch Regulations, and submitted for approval and implementation. The training expenses shall be paid by the province. (Article 7) All people's surcharges, special donations, special allocations, and all county-owned properties in autonomous counties shall be included in the entire revenue of the budget案, and shall be disbursed separately in accordance with legally prescribed procedures. (Article 8) The autonomous counties shall be subsidized by the provincial government from the regular grain tax payable by the counties. (Article 9) In the distribution of all autonomous county expenditures, administrative expenses must not exceed two-tenths of business expenses. (Article 10) Residents of autonomous counties, in addition to the regular land tax, are absolutely not obligated to pay any taxes or donations that are not listed in the budget mentioned in Article 7 or declared by the state. (Article 11) The current security group system in autonomous counties shall be revoked or corrected by the provincial government upon consulting with the anti-bandit headquarters after the county magistrate decides on a public security plan in accordance with Article 4 of this plan and submits it for approval. (Article 12) If the county government of an autonomous county needs to reduce the scope of its affairs and expenses due to the establishment of district offices, the county magistrate may handle it in accordance with Article 16, Paragraph 2 of the County Organization Law. Chapter 2, Finance. (Article 13) The financial administration of autonomous counties must formulate budget案 for each level of agency in accordance with the autonomous administrative plan, and all procedures must be in accordance with legally prescribed procedures. (Article 14) The budget案 mentioned in the preceding article shall be compiled by a temporary county financial budget committee composed of the county financial authorities (including the Director of the Finance Bureau and members of the Finance Committee) and the responsible persons recommended by the meeting mentioned in Article 4 of this plan, and submitted to the county magistrate for approval before implementation. (Article 15) Autonomous counties shall collect and remit national taxes, and the county government may order agencies at all levels to collect and remit them in the same way as before for agencies established for the collection of national taxes. Chapter 3, Education. (Article 16) Autonomous counties must not divert education funds that have been determined in the past for other purposes. (Article 17) The education funds mentioned in the preceding article, regardless of their source and type, must all be included in the total budget案, and the county government and agencies below the county government shall manage the revenue and expenditure in accordance with the law. (Article 18) The education plans and implementation of autonomous counties shall be newly stipulated in accordance with Article 4 of this plan, and special attention must be paid to rural mass education. (Article 19) Autonomous counties must establish special education research associations and education research branch associations to earnestly study and improve local education and implement it as soon as possible. The methods shall be drafted by a temporary education conference organized by the county education authorities (including the Director of the Education Bureau and the Chairman of the Education Association) and the responsible persons recommended by the conference mentioned in Article 4, and submitted to the county magistrate for approval before implementation. (Article 20) Education in autonomous counties shall pay special attention to the inherent morality of the nation and production skills. (Article 21) If, due to a lack of teachers or other matters, the established schools are indeed in need of improvement, they may be temporarily suspended, and the funds that have been allocated shall still be managed by the statutory agencies in the usual manner, and efforts shall be made to find ways to provide relief and improvement. Chapter 4, Public Security. (Article 22) Public security matters in autonomous counties must be based on the facilities of autonomy at all levels. (Article 23) The public security administration of autonomous counties must emphasize both rural and urban areas to ensure that all county residents can live and work in peace in the countryside. (Article 24) Public security plans in autonomous counties must comply with the intent of the County Defense Corps Law and combine it with the actual local conditions. The plans shall be drafted by a temporary public security conference organized by the county public security authorities (including the Director of the Public Security Bureau, the Commander of the Security Corps, and the Commander of the Volunteer General Brigade) and the responsible persons recommended by the conference mentioned in Article 4, and submitted to the county magistrate for approval before implementation. Chapter 5, Construction. (Article 25) The construction of autonomous counties must be increased year by year, and the distribution of all autonomous funds must be increased year by year for construction projects. (Article 26) The construction of autonomous counties should especially focus on rural undertakings, and the most necessary ones are as follows: supervising and organizing arable land, revitalizing ditches and water conservancy, fully developing forestry, promoting agricultural and forestry auxiliary industries, building roads and bridges, and building various factories. (Article 27) The implementation of construction projects must focus on those that are productive and economic. Chapter 6, Economy. (Article 28) Autonomous counties must pay special attention to developing the rural economy. (Article 29) In accordance with the purpose mentioned in the preceding article, the county government must supervise agencies at all levels to implement the following projects: promotion and adjustment of agricultural products, improvement and protection of industry and commerce, and organization and promotion of cooperatives. (November 26)

Wuxi

Tax Bureau Arbitrarily Confiscates Cigarettes, Leading to Disputes

Several cigarette shops in this county, including Fuxing Yongxingchang Yitaifeng and Xincheng Shuxia Xiexingsheng Xintaiheng, all sell "Little Champagne" cigarettes produced by Shanghai Dadong Tobacco Company. Sales have been fairly good. However, a few days ago, several officials from the General Taxation Bureau suddenly went to these shops, confiscated the "Little Champagne" cigarettes, and claimed they were counterfeit. Afterward, the shops sent a letter to the Tobacco Exchange Association, which immediately convened a temporary meeting. Chairman Chen Nianzhu presided over the meeting and the following resolutions were made: 1. Notify all shops to temporarily stop selling "Little Champagne" cigarettes. 2. Before the investigation by the General Taxation Bureau is resolved, all "Little Champagne" cigarettes should be returned to the management office to avoid accidental losses. 3. Appoint responsible personnel to handle negotiations. 4. Send a letter to the Chamber of Commerce to inquire about the reasons for the confiscation by the General Taxation Bureau.

Grain Piles Up Awaiting Transport to Tianjin by Train

In the past, grain transport on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway was limited to diverting shipments from Nanjing to stations like Pingxi and Shanghai. The source was mostly rice produced in Anhui and northern Jiangsu provinces, flowing south in large quantities. The saying was, "The northwest can never be emptied, and the southeast can never be filled." Today, the situation is completely different, the opposite of before. Large quantities of grain are now being transported to Nanjing, crossing the river, and then transported by the Jinpu Railway to Jinan and Tianjin for delivery. This is because Jinan and Tianjin are currently experiencing grain shortages, and rice prices are higher than in Xidi (Wuxi), making it profitable to transport grain there. Therefore, merchants from those two ports have been continuously coming to Wuxi to purchase grain recently, which has led to a slight increase in rice prices. However, the number of locomotives on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is insufficient, and there is also a shortage of freight cars, resulting in the accumulation of grain in both the new and old freight depots at Wuxi Station. The piles are so high that they are touching the roofs, leaving no room for maneuver. Moreover, barges are still arriving from Hexia to deposit grain in the warehouses, all waiting for transport by train. Even with the new cargo transport regulations that stipulate a 30% increase in freight charges for priority shipping, it is still difficult to dispatch trains for transport at any time, causing great anxiety among grain merchants. Furthermore, Wuxi had a good rice harvest this year. As of today, the amount of rice stored in the various grain depots is about 70% of capacity, mostly stored by merchants planning to transport it to the northwest market next year in hopes of making a profit. Currently, high-quality white rice sells for 7.2 yuan per stone. Without merchant hoarding, market prices might fall. If grain can circulate freely within the country, it could still sell for 9 or 10 yuan per stone next year. However, if domestic circulation is hindered and transport to Tianjin and Jinan is inconvenient, there will be no hope for rising rice prices. Therefore, the future trend of rice in Jiangsu and Zhejiang will depend on free circulation.

Nantong

Water Police Seize Large Quantity of Opium

At Nantong Tianshenggang, at the end of last month, the Water Police Corps seized a very large quantity of imported opium. Except for a portion marked as belonging to the "Xinjin Company," the rest was unmarked. It has been detained. This matter has attracted great attention from the local people.

Dispute over Settlement of Public Education Funds

The public education funds of Nantong were deposited for interest. Due to the conversion of copper coins into silver dollars, there has been a long-standing dispute with the pawnshops. Later, the pawnshops agreed to a conversion rate of 1,460 copper coins to one silver dollar and additionally donated 7,300 yuan to the charity fund as a settlement, which was reported to the province for record. Now the pawnshops have broken the agreement, and the Education Bureau has petitioned the county to recover the funds.

In Baimazhen, a town under the county's jurisdiction, a group of more than 80 bandits suddenly arrived the night before last, each carrying rifles and pistols, and two machine guns. The garrisoned troops in the town, due to the overwhelming number of bandits, did not dare to resist and allowed the bandits to shout and escape.

Embankment and Canal Construction Along Fields Not Considered Official Property

To protect farmland and increase rural by-products, it should not be considered within the scope of official property. An announcement was also posted to inform the public. They earnestly request that the aforementioned resolution be implemented to alleviate the people's hardship. Page 11

Northeast Merchants Shut Down Businesses and Head South

Recognizing National Goods as Foreign Goods Forces Chinese to Easily Change Nationality

The Result of Japanese Military and Economic Aggression

Chinese People, Quickly Rise Up! Swiftly Plan How to Restore Your Businesses!

Since the Japanese occupied our Northeast, they have used the same tactics they used to subjugate Korea, gradually seizing our finances, occupying our markets, and further abusing our people. Recently, Chinese merchants in the Northeast, unable to bear the heavy taxes and levies, have been shutting down their businesses and heading south. A reporter met a traveler from Fengtian (Mukden) to Shanghai who described in detail the suffering of the Chinese people in the Northeast and the brutal treatment of those going to the south by the Japanese. A report has been written as follows.

National Goods Disappear Since September 25th, when the puppet state forcibly occupied the Northeast customs, goods from our country shipped from ports such as Shanghai and Tianjin have been regarded as foreign goods and subject to taxation. Dalian was originally a free port and did not collect taxes on imported goods. Therefore, foreign goods shipped to Dalian were mostly transshipped through Shanghai, where they were taxed by the Jianghai Customs once. Now the Japanese have persuaded European and American countries to ship goods to Dalian directly without going through Shanghai, which avoids import taxes. As a result, Dalian is flooded with foreign goods, and prices are even cheaper. Chinese goods have been almost completely driven out by foreign goods. Throughout the three northeastern provinces, there are only foreign goods and Japanese goods; Chinese goods have almost disappeared.

Chinese Merchants Close Down Businesses Chinese businesses in Liaoning, Yingkou, Andong, Dalian, and Changchun were very large. Merchants dealing in silk, native cloth, and local and imported goods could be found everywhere. Since September 25th, domestically produced silk fabrics, cotton fabrics, and local goods have suddenly disappeared and cannot be transported there. The main reason is that merchants from the Northeast cannot purchase them. When domestically produced goods reach the Northeast, they are subject to heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies, causing the value of Chinese goods to rise several times, and silk fabrics have even become impossible to import. Since this month, merchants in the Northeast have been shutting down their businesses and returning south. The market for silk and cotton fabrics has been completely taken over by Japanese goods. In recent days, more than 400 merchants have arrived from Fengtian, Yingkou, Dalian, and other places in the south. Most of the passengers on the Fengtian Maru and Dalian Maru to Shanghai are these southern merchants. It is said that another thousand people will continue to return south soon.

The Japanese are Ferocious Everywhere in the Northeast, there are volunteer armies. The Japanese forces are only along the railway. The Japanese in the Northeast are most afraid of attacks by the volunteer army. Therefore, recently, the Japanese have been extremely strict in their searches and inquiries of Chinese people arriving at Dalian, Yingkou, and Andong by ship from the south or Tianjin. Any hesitation or slow response is immediately arrested, and there is no return. The Japanese regard every Chinese person going to the Northeast as a volunteer army. Without a solid guarantee from local shops and residents, it is difficult to enter. At the Dalian pier, many Chinese are arrested every time a ship arrives from Shanghai. Therefore, it is hoped that Chinese people will not go there unless they have urgent matters or have acquaintances. It is feared they will only lose their lives in vain.

Forcibly Changing Nationality Residents of the Northeast have been forced by the Japanese not to use the word "Chinese" anymore. All documents or external communications must be written in the "Manchukuo" style, or they will be fined. This time, dozens of merchants from Fengtian, including Chen Jinrong, Lin Yishi, Lin Xijiu, and Feng Yangkong, came to Shanghai. When buying boat tickets, the Japanese forced them to write "Manchukuo" and not "China." This is the first time that Chinese people have come to Shanghai in the name of "Manchukuo."

The Municipal Self-Government Preparatory Committee Sets the Work Procedure

District Offices to be Established within this Month

Self-Government to be Completed Next Year

The Municipal Self-Government Preparatory Committee has been actively working since its establishment on July 1 this year. The committee has now set a work schedule to complete various tasks within a set time frame. A summary is listed below: From July 1 to December 31, 21st year [1932], establish the committee, design the progress of various operations, stipulate the applicable regulations and laws, and establish 40 district offices, install boundary markers in each district, and complete the most basic tasks. From January 1 to February 28, 22nd year [1933], conduct household registration and verification in each district. From March 1 to April 15, conduct a full city census and random checks, administer citizen oaths, and submit a detailed list of candidates for district chiefs, district people's representatives, and ward supervisors to the municipal government for announcement and district notice. From April 16 to April 20, announce the list of candidates at all levels. If there are no applications for rectification or reports of omissions within the time limit, it will be considered final. From April 21 to May 31, divide each district into wards, neighborhoods, and lanes, and clearly mark all ward, neighborhood, and lane signs. Submit the details to the municipal government and then to the Ministry of Interior for record. From June 1 to June 15, begin the election of ward chiefs and complete the election of ward chiefs in 40 districts. From June 16 to June 30, hold the election of neighborhood chiefs and complete the election of neighborhood chiefs in 40 districts. From July 1 to July 15, continue with the election of lane chiefs, and the election of ward chiefs, neighborhood chiefs, and lane chiefs will be completely completed. From July 16 to July 31, each district will convene a ward meeting to establish a ward office, elect a ward supervisor and a mediation committee, and establish a ward supervisory committee and a ward mediation committee. From August 1 to August 15, all elections below the ward level will be completed. The committee will report the details to the municipal government and submit a list of elected officials to the Ministry of Interior for record. From August 16 to August 31, the Ministry of Interior will send personnel to inspect and approve the popular election of district chiefs. From September 1 to November 15, hold the election of district chiefs and elect district people's representatives. Convene the first district people's representative assembly and elect district supervisors. All levels of self-government below the district level will be fully prepared. From November 16 to November 31, dismiss the appointed district chiefs and personnel preparing for self-government at all levels and establish elected offices. From December 1 to December 31, complete the dissolution of the committee. The committee's preparatory tasks will be completed at this point.

Wu Chao-chu Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

Talks About How North China Is a Land of Resources but Lacks Personnel

The Resolution of the Sino-Japanese Problem Lies in Our Own Strength

Will Attend the Third Plenary Session and is Currently Drafting a Proposal

Member of the Central Committee, Mr. Wu Chao-chu, along with his wife, traveled to Tianjin and the Northwest for more than a month and arrived in Shanghai by night train from Beijing yesterday morning. The reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Wu at his residence yesterday morning and was granted an interview. During the conversation, he said, "My trip to the north was purely for travel and had no other mission. Although Tianjin is a place I have visited before, it has been sixteen years since I last went there, and I had never been to the Northwest. Therefore, this trip to the north was to observe the recent conditions in North China. This trip lasted more than a month and took me through Ping, Tianjin, Datong, Suiyuan, Baotou, Dingxian, Luoyang, Xi'an, Kaifeng, and Xuzhou. The north is a land of resources, but it lacks talent, resulting in treasures being left underground and the rural economy bankrupt. For example, Shaanxi was originally a fertile area, but due to the lack of water conservancy facilities, it has suffered years of famine. During my visit, I saw thousands of miles of barren land and deserted villages, like entering the Mongolian desert. It is truly lamentable. The people of the north are diligent and simple, but their knowledge is not as good as that of the people of the south. The anti-Japanese sentiment in the north is also very depressed, not as tense as in the south. The League of Nations will convene a meeting to discuss the Sino-Japanese problem. However, we cannot predict how the League of Nations will ultimately resolve the Sino-Japanese problem. The League of Nations is not a supreme government. The League of Nations does not have the power to solve the Sino-Japanese problem by itself. The League of Nations relies on the member states and the great powers for its power. Currently, it is very unclear and unpredictable what the attitude of the United Kingdom, France, the United States, and Russia is towards the Sino-Japanese problem. Therefore, it is difficult to predict how the League of Nations will resolve the Sino-Japanese problem. The League of Nations' invitation to the United States and Russia to participate and express their opinions is also a way for the League of Nations to increase its own strength. If our country's internal affairs are well managed, diplomacy will naturally have a solution. The Third Plenary Session has been scheduled to be held in Beijing on the 15th. I will go to attend and am currently drafting a proposal, focusing on improving internal affairs. As I have said, with well-managed internal affairs, diplomacy will naturally have a solution. I have no knowledge of whether members of the Central Committee from Guangdong will attend the Third Plenary Session or have any proposals. Although I met Mr. Feng Huanzhang in Zhangjiakou, I do not know whether he will attend the Third Plenary Session or have any proposals. As for Mr. Feng's views on internal affairs and diplomacy, they are still the same as those reported in previous reports and telegrams of Mr. Feng's talks."
