Aftermath of the Japanese Police Arresting People Across the Border

Although Kim Young-taek has been Released, the Japanese Consul Still Demands Detention, Taxpayers' Association Sends a Letter Requesting Protection

On the night of the 30th, plainclothes police officers from the Japanese Consulate illegally arrested Korean Kim Young-taek Kim Cheol at No. 2 Ruyi Lane, Rue Victor Emmanuel III in the French Concession. The French police detained two Japanese policemen, causing negotiations. Although the arrested were exchanged and released the night before last, the French authorities say that this is not the first time that Japanese plainclothes police have arrested people across the border, so they are still collecting evidence for negotiations.

Exchanged and Released the Night Before Last

After the consulate's plainclothes police officers crossed the border and arrested Kim Cheol, two other policemen, Aioiyama and Yamazaki, continued to arrest Kim Cheol. They were detained by the police station. The next day, the French Consulate made a serious protest to the Japanese side. The Japanese side released Kim Cheol and sent him to the French police station at 6 o'clock the night before last. After Kim arrived, the police station released the two Japanese policemen at 7 o'clock.

Kim Cheol was Beaten and Injured

After Kim was arrested and taken to the Japanese Consulate's police department, his head, face, and fingers were beaten and injured. The reporter from the Guowen News Agency met Kim's wife yesterday. According to her, "When my husband returned, his fingers were injured by handcuffs, and both hands were swollen. There were also bruises on his head and face from the beatings. He is currently receiving treatment somewhere. As for the internal injuries, I do not know because the doctor has not yet issued a medical certificate."

Naturalization Certificate Sent to France

The reporter from the Guowen News Agency also went to Cai Xiaobai, the lawyer who handled Kim's naturalization as a Chinese citizen in 1929, to inquire. According to him, "Kim is indeed a Korean who has been naturalized as a Chinese citizen. He has now been released and there should be no major problem. However, the French authorities have requested to review Kim's naturalization documents from the past and sent them to the French Embassy for submission to the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs for review and then return them. Now that Kim is indeed a Chinese citizen, the Chinese government should protect him."

News from the French Consulate

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the French Consulate is still unwilling to make any official statement on this matter but stated in a private capacity that the consulate considers it unnecessary to make any further demands because the Japanese consul has expressed his apologies. The reporter asked what the French side would do if the Japanese sent someone to arrest Kim again. The person replied, "If the Japanese arrest someone, the French side can arrest them according to the law." Then, they were asked whether they were Korean. If they thought he was Korean, they would extradite him to the Japanese Consulate for investigation. Otherwise, it would depend on the instructions of the French Minister.

Oral Protest from the Municipal Government

Since the incident occurred, the municipal government has made oral protests to both the French and Japanese authorities as Kim Cheol is Chinese. However, since he has now been released and the matter is over, it is currently under consideration whether to continue protesting to the other party to ensure future protection.

Important Letter from the Taxpayers' Association

The French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the French Consul General and the Police Department, saying, "We are writing to you to report that the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai has dispatched secret agents to illegally arrest residents of the French Concession without following legal procedures or international conventions. Your authorities have resisted according to the law, and the Japanese Consulate has apologized, which is admirable. All residents unanimously praise this. It has been found that the Japanese authorities rely on their superior military force, disregard international conventions, disregard the law, and disregard all countries, almost to the point where everyone dares not argue with them. After your authorities gave them a considerable lesson in the face of unbearable circumstances, it may make them restrain themselves a little, and the residents of the French Concession may be a little relieved. However, there is still no guarantee that the same incident will not happen again in the future. Because their attitude is changeable, it is still not enough to provide a real guarantee for the residents of the French Concession. Therefore, in addition to expressing our respect, we are writing to request that your authorities obtain a guarantee from the Japanese Consulate that the same incident will not happen again in the future to reassure the residents. This is the public's feeling. Respectfully submitted to Mr. Meili Ai, the French Consul General in Shanghai. The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession.

The Japanese Consul Will Still Arrest Him

According to the Da Mei Evening News, it is reported that the Japanese Consulate is still planning to issue an arrest warrant for Kim Cheol and his nephew Kim Cheol and send it to the French Consulate, requesting them to arrest him and hand him over to the Japanese authorities. Although the date has not been announced, it must not be far away.

Suma Disregards Sovereignty

Suma, an intelligence officer at the Japanese Consulate, spoke with a reporter from the Shanghai Times, admitting that the Japanese police's forceful arrest of Kim Cheol was a major mistake, but said that they did not intend to infringe on the rights of the French Concession authorities and that the mistake was really due to mistaking the French Concession for the Chinese Concession. He claimed that the Chinese and Japanese authorities had previously agreed that the Japanese authorities could take action against any Japanese criminal residing in the Chinese Concession. The translator believes that Suma's words are ridiculous, and his claim that the Japanese authorities can arrest any Japanese criminal residing in the Chinese Concession at will shows that he has no regard for Chinese sovereignty.

Korean Shops are in Danger

According to the Continental News, Korean residents in the French Concession report that Japanese plainclothes detectives have been very active among Korean residents recently. Detectives enter Korean-owned shops almost every day under the pretext of inquiring about prices. They all speak fluent Korean. There are even several shops that are constantly being secretly monitored by the Japanese. These people are obviously detectives. Therefore, many Korean patrons are afraid and dare not come forward. As for the real reason why the Japanese detectives are so active, it is still unknown. It is speculated that it is because after the Japanese army forcibly occupied Manchuria and was fiercely resisted by the volunteer army, they feared that the Korean independence movement would also take the opportunity to intensify, so they stepped up their efforts. News from Korea is rarely transmitted abroad due to strict Japanese inspections, but according to a few brief messages that have fortunately leaked out, many Koreans are currently assisting the Northeast Volunteer Army inside or outside Korea.

Huang Zhanrong Has Fled into Hiding

Guangdong native Huang Zhanrong's appointment with Kim seems to indicate a conspiracy to arrest the Kim father and son. Although there is no serious crime, the French police are still investigating Huang to clarify the situation and any suspicion of a premeditated conspiracy in this case to verify. But Huang has now fled into hiding, and it is rumored that Huang is now sheltered by a certain Japanese person in Hongkou and does not leave his home.

The Silk and Satin Trade Associations Urgently Request the Government to Sign a Commercial Treaty Between China, France, and Vietnam

Overseas Chinese are in a treaty-less state, causing the silk industry to stagnate and hinder foreign sales

The Shanghai Electrical Silk Weaving Factory Trade Association held a banquet on the 17th of last month to welcome the two representatives from Vietnam returning to China, Huang and Xu, and invited the Silk and Satin Trade Association to express their willingness to assist, as reported previously. Now, it is heard that the two associations have jointly submitted a petition to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and sent a letter to Gu Shaochuan, the special envoy stationed in France, urging him to negotiate with the French government as soon as possible to sign a commercial treaty between China, France, and Vietnam. The goal is to alleviate the suffering of overseas Chinese who are in a treaty-less state and to promote the export of silk products. They have also sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting their assistance, hoping to achieve diplomatic success in the shortest possible time. The petition to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is recorded below: The petition is regarding the fact that the China-France-Vietnam commercial treaty has not been signed, which has severely impacted the export of Chinese silk to Annam. We earnestly request that you promptly negotiate with the French government to expedite the signing of a special treaty between China and Vietnam, and immediately include domestic silk products in the most-favored-nation tariff treatment, to benefit overseas Chinese and maintain international trade. Since our government established its capital and implemented revolutionary diplomacy, in the 17th year of the Republic of China, it notified the envoys of various countries stationed in China to negotiate equal treaties to facilitate commercial development and strengthen diplomatic ties between the two countries. Sino-Vietnamese trade has historically been prosperous due to historical relations. Silk and medicinal materials are the most exported goods from China to Annam, and the tax rates enjoyed are also quite favorable. Vietnam and China signed the first special commercial treaty between China and France on June 26, 1887. At that time, Vietnam only levied 200 francs for every 100 kilograms of Chinese silk imports. Later, it gradually increased from 400 francs to 600 francs. The Qing government was ignorant of diplomacy and did not know how to protect foreign trade, so the French did whatever they wanted and repeatedly increased the tax. In the first half of the 17th year of the Republic of China, it increased to 1,360 francs per 100 kilograms. Each kilogram was valued at 17.5 yuan, with a tax of 1.225 yuan, equivalent to 7%. The then Minister of Foreign Affairs, Wang, declared that in order to implement tariff autonomy, the Sino-French Land Trade Regulations and the Sino-French Continued Commercial Treaty, which were signed before July 7 of the 17th year of the Republic of China, were abolished on the day the Sino-French Continued Commercial Treaty expired. Negotiations began on December 23 of the 17th year of the Republic of China, but no decision has been reached for a long time. The French side believes that since the old treaty has been abolished and the new treaty has not been signed, all silk exported from China to Annam will be treated as goods from a treaty-less country. The Annam government suddenly announced a new import tariff for silk, as follows per 100 kilograms:

Commodity Name: Normal Tariff Most Favored Nation Tariff

White Silk: 16,000 Francs 4,000 Francs

Colored Silk: 10,000 Francs 2,500 Francs

Colored/White Smooth Silk: 11,000 Francs 2,500 Francs

Colored/White Shiny Smooth Silk: 14,000 Francs 3,750 Francs

In the past, China levied 200 francs per 100 kilograms according to the most-favored-nation tariff regulations of the old treaty, but the actual levy was 1,360 francs. Since the announcement of this tariff, paying taxes according to the normal tariff rate has increased from 7% to 50%. Chinese merchants have been greatly affected and are in great pain. Although the former Minister of Foreign Affairs, Wang, protested to the French Ambassador to China, Mad, it has had no effect. Recently, it has been learned that Japan has signed a commercial treaty with Vietnam. On August 28th of this year, the Vietnamese government announced reciprocal tariffs for Japanese goods, with more than 100 items, of which silk is an important part. From then on, Japanese goods can be sold in large quantities, while Chinese silk cannot be sold due to high taxes. In the past, our country's silk sold well in Annam because of the protection of tariffs, and Japan was in a normal position, so Chinese silk could still compete for a short time. Now, our country has retreated to a normal position. It is feared that from now on, not a single strand of silk will be seen in Annam. In the past, our country's silk exports to Annam amounted to 30 million yuan per year under the old tariff, of which 15 million yuan were exported from the Shanghai Customs and 15 million yuan were exported from the Guangzhou Customs. This huge amount of silk is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Since the implementation of the new tariff, the domestic silk weaving industry has plummeted, factories have closed down, and workers have lost their jobs, which is very painful. Overseas Chinese in Vietnam used to rely on the silk trade for their livelihoods, but now they are suffering from the treatment of a treaty-less country, and their businesses have plummeted. The actual situation has already been reported by the recently returned representatives Huang and Xu, so there is no need to repeat it. Therefore, the signing of the Vietnamese commercial treaty is like looking forward to rain during a severe drought, both domestically and abroad. Therefore, we jointly submit this petition, hoping that you will review it and expedite the signing of a commercial treaty between China and Vietnam in the shortest possible time, and include silk in the most-favored-nation tariff treatment according to the old treaty, to care for overseas merchants and maintain international silk trade. We are extremely apprehensive and await your orders. The letters to Special Envoy Gu and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce are roughly the same, and are not recorded here.

Zhang Yuejun's Talk After the Public Telegram

There were prior contacts with representatives from Sichuan

Sichuan generals have telegraphed their support

A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Zhang Qun, a member of the Central Committee, yesterday and asked about the response from the generals in Sichuan after the public telegram was sent. Mr. Zhang described the circumstances before and after the telegram was issued in great detail, as follows: Before I (Mr. Zhang referred to himself as such below) issued the public telegram advocating for it, I had considerable contact with representatives from various parties in Sichuan in Beijing and Hankou. The generals Liu (Xiang), Liu (Wenhui), Deng (Xihou), Tian (Songyao), and Liu (Cunhou) all expressed their support. Yesterday's report that Wang Fangzhou was sent to Hankou by Liu Fu Cheng (Xiang) to oppose the Reorganization Committee is completely untrue, as Fu Cheng telegraphed his representatives on the 27th expressing his support. As for whether the Central Government will adopt my proposal, it is still unknown. This matter must wait until it is adopted before we can discuss how to organize it. Who will be in charge is a secondary matter. The Hankou communication reported that I sent a letter to a certain Sichuanese gentleman in Hankou, and did not indicate a desire to resign from the position of Chairman of the Reorganization Committee. In fact, I have repeatedly and clearly stated that I do not want to hold any position. After handing over my duties as Mayor of Shanghai this year, the Central Government repeatedly asked me to take up a position in Beijing, but I did not agree. This summer, when I was in Beiping, there were various speculations about me, but I ultimately declined the position of member of the Military Affairs Committee Branch. There have been many similar instances this year, all of which I have declined. How could I be interested in a position in Sichuan? There is no question of going to Sichuan. Moreover, the cook manages the kitchen, and should not think of dipping his fingers in it. The poor girl sews the thread, and does not add makeup. It would be ridiculous to say that I proposed setting up the Reorganization Committee because I intended to participate in it. It is a fact that I cannot ignore the affairs of Sichuan because of my relationship with my hometown, and that's all, he said.

Reactions to the Ministry of Railways' Land Grab

Declaration by the Flower and Tree Trade Association

The Shanghai Flower and Tree Trade Association issued a statement to all sectors of society yesterday regarding the Ministry of Railways' requisition of land in Zhaojia Garden and other villages in the Pengpu District. The statement reads: According to letters from Zhao Youting, Youqi, Yuntang, and others, executive committee members of the Zhaojia Garden, Zhu Lane, and Flower and Tree Trade Association in the Pengpu District of Shanghai, the Ministry of Railways is requisitioning land to build a joint transportation station. After the plan was changed, 1,400 mu of land originally located west of Zhongshan Road and south of Jiaotong Road was given up, and 700 mu east of it to Zhaojia Garden was suddenly added, completely requisitioning all the land where villagers, households, populations, flowers, and trees are concentrated. This will cause the people of the area to be displaced, homeless, and without land to cultivate, turning them into starving people. They have no way to appeal and earnestly request that you take measures to rescue them. Our association believes that this matter concerns our industry and will hinder the prosperity of Shanghai. We convened an executive committee meeting to discuss it. Everyone agreed that the matter is serious and that we must strive to give up the entire Zhaojia Garden village to maintain the people's livelihoods. We have submitted a detailed report, hoping that all sectors of society will pay attention to it. The flower and tree industry in Shanghai is a necessity for society, contributing to the prosperity of the city and the cultural and material well-being of the country. The villages of Zhaojia Garden and Zhu Lane account for four-fifths of the city's flower and tree supply. How can they be arbitrarily destroyed and eradicated? Zhaojia Garden in the Pengpu District of northern Shanghai has interconnected fields covering more than a thousand mu. It is green all year round. Since its cultivation nearly 200 years ago, it has had millions of flowers and trees, large and small. Among them are rare flowers and exotic species that have been cultivated for four or five years, or cultivated for forty or fifty years, to achieve one-tenth of the profit. Thus, fathers pass on the business to their sons, and grandsons continue it. All the villagers, more than 500 households with thousands of people, rely on it for their livelihood and have lived in peace for hundreds of years. The flowers, fruits, and plants admired by Chinese and foreigners in Shanghai also rely heavily on the products of Zhaojia Garden. However, the Ministry of Railways, in its plan to build a joint transportation station, disregards the people's livelihood and arbitrarily requisitions the historical and valuable gardens of Zhaojia Garden, causing all the villagers to lose their skills and work, and greatly affecting the decline of our industry. If we say that we should move to another place, we should know that trees with deep roots and solid foundations are not suitable for soil and are not easy to plant, unlike rice and wheat, which can be sown anywhere. After the requisition, the land price in the vicinity will increase, which is beyond the reach of the people's ability. If we say that we should compensate for the price, we should know that it is not the work of one day or one night. Those who cultivate this have lost the basics of their livelihood. How will an eight-member family survive within ten years? Moreover, since the Qi-Lu War, there have been frequent wars. Those who survived the disaster are already scarred. If they want to move again, they will be displaced. Not to mention anything else, considering that our late Premier Sun Yat-sen's outline for nation-building considers agriculture and forestry to be the most important aspects of the people's livelihood and should be promoted and protected, so as not to go against the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's legacy. Now, the Ministry of Railways is acting perversely, which is unexpected. Our association believes that the Ministry of Railways' requisition of all the people's land in Zhaojia Garden and Zhu Lane is a great damage to the interests of the people and an obstacle to the development of our association's business. We are deeply concerned and have to state our grievances in detail so that our compatriots from all walks of life can know the truth. We respectfully ask all sectors to show sympathy, provide assistance, and ensure that the Ministry of Railways withdraws its order and finds a way to avoid it, so as to relieve the people's difficulties and maintain the people's livelihoods. Otherwise, all the villagers will vow to fight to the death, and the members of our association will not remain silent. We plead with all our hearts, and hope for your public appraisal.

Reorganization of China National Aviation Corporation

Dai Enji Succeeds as General Manager

After Zhu Jia-hua succeeded as Minister of Communications, the Chinese shareholders of China National Aviation Corporation dispatched the Director of the Aviation Administration, Gao Tingzi, the Director of the Postal Administration, Lin Shi, and Weng Zhilong and Shen Shihua as representatives. Yesterday, the company held a shareholders' meeting and a board meeting to carry out reorganization matters. The details are as follows:

Shareholders' Meeting: After the reorganization, the company held a new shareholders' meeting at its offices at 10:00 AM yesterday. The new Chinese shareholder representatives, Lin Shi, Gao Tingzi, Shen Shihua, and Weng Zhilong, and the American representatives, Band, Plin, and Harkins, attended the meeting. Zhu Jiahua, Dai Enji, Huang Naishu, and Shen Shihua were elected as directors, among whom Huang Naishu was re-elected.

Board Meeting: After the directors were elected, the eighteenth board meeting was held at the same place at 3:00 PM yesterday. Time of Assuming Office: Mr. Dai Enji, who was appointed as the general manager, is currently in the capital. After being elected, the company immediately notified him by telegram. It is said that Mr. Dai is scheduled to come to Shanghai this Sunday (i.e., tomorrow) and will come to the company to assume his duties on Monday next week.

Closing of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association

A total of more than 1.4 million in relief was distributed

Establishment of a Disaster Prevention Association

The Jiangsu Flood Relief Association has been raising funds for flood relief for many years and has now ended. The closing ceremony was held at the Renji Hall yesterday. The committee members Wang Yiting, Li Qiqing, Ha Shaofu, Zhu Xiechen, Cheng Jingsheng, Huang Hanzhi, Wu Yunzhai, and more than 30 others attended the ceremony. Wang Yiting, the chairman, reported on the relief situation over the past year and the closing situation (report from the General Affairs Group). The relief area covers 48 counties, with approximately 1.9 million people receiving relief. A total of 1,427,200 yuan was distributed. The relief funds received included 338,000 yuan allocated by the Provincial Relief Affairs Association, 35,788 yuan from the interest of the Construction Public Bonds, 82,000 yuan allocated by the Administrative Yuan Emergency Relief Commissioner, and 4,000 yuan allocated by the Relief Affairs Committee. The above belongs to the official funds, totaling 460,088 yuan. The remaining 967,157 yuan were all from the association's fundraising, donations from charitable organizations, and privately raised funds. A record of these relief funds has been printed. The existing Construction Public Bonds have a face value of 244,400 yuan. Upon the temporary proposal of Committee Member Li Qiqing, Committee Member Ha Shaofu, and Committee Member Huang Hanzhi, although the flood relief work in the province has been completed, attention should still be paid to disaster prevention work in the future. It was decided to establish the Jiangsu Disaster Prevention Association to properly plan. The Jiangsu Flood Relief Association will be reorganized, and Huang Hanzhi, Cheng Jingsheng, Li Qiqing, Zhu Xiechen, Ha Shaofu, Wu Yunzhai, Hu Bijang, Zhu Yinjiang, Wen Lanting, Weng Yinchu, Gu Jisheng, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaoliang, Xi Yunsheng, Wang Yiting, Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, Wang Shuxiang, and Leng Yuqiu were appointed as committee members. Subsequently, Wu Yunzhai, Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Li Qiqing, and Cheng Jingsheng were mutually elected as standing committee members, and Wang Yiting was elected as the chairman, and Huang Hanzhi and Cheng Jingsheng were elected as the vice chairmen. The General Affairs Group proposed a plan for the storage of the Construction Public Bonds after the association is dissolved. It was decided that the Disaster Prevention Association should be responsible for the storage, and the bonds should still be stored in the salt industry bank vault.

A Record of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee's Inspection of Completed Dike Projects (5)

(Inspection of the Second District) The dike project in the second district, on the south bank of the Yangtze River, stretches from Heshang Port in Dangtu County to X溝 in Tongling County. On the north bank, it stretches from Wujiang in He County to Zhangjiaba in Tongcheng County. The total length of the dike is 335.3 kilometers. The total amount of earthwork completed is 3,329,357 cubic meters. The total cost is 128,066.62 yuan. The total number of disaster relief workers is 84,350. Therefore, the dike project in the second district is more extensive than that in the first district. Moreover, the 600-zhang dike project in Tongcheng County on the north bank has not yet been completed and is currently being rushed to completion with approximately 3,000 workers. According to the scheduled inspection procedure, at 8:20 AM on the 29th, a small boat will be used to inspect: (1) Sihushan to Yijishan, in Yanhu County on the south bank; (2) Wuhu to Lugang, in Wuhu County on the south bank. At 10:00 AM, the main ship and small boat will be used to inspect: (3) Huangsitan, in Wuwei County on the north bank. At 12:30 PM, return to the main ship. At 2:30 PM, a small boat will be used to inspect: (4) Daijialongtan, in Wuwei County on the north bank. At 3:30 PM, return to the main ship to inspect: (5) Bagentou, in Tonglu County on the south bank; (6) Liubai Zhang, in Tongcheng County on the north bank. However, due to time constraints, only (1) Sihushan to Yijishan, (2) Wuhu to Lugang, and (3) Huangsitan were inspected.

(Situation of the Xijiang Embankment) The Lihu small boat of the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission rushed from Shanghai to Wuhu on the morning of the 29th. The entire inspection team transferred to the Lihu small boat at 8:30 AM on the same day and first inspected the Xijiang embankment downstream of the south bank of Wuhu. The embankment is between Sihushan and Yijishan. The old embankment is on the riverside, and most of it has collapsed, leaving only traces. The new embankment is about a li away, with a top width of about four meters. The embankment surface is uneven, and there are several large holes. It has only been completed for several months, but it is already like this. This must be due to the hasty construction. Who knows what it will be like in a year? Xu Shiying and Wen Lanting accompanied the inspection. Although they are old, they walk very quickly and are admirable. At 10:00 AM, they returned to the small boat and sailed upstream of Wuhu to inspect the Mapu embankment project between Wuhu and Lugang. Mapu is only a few li away from Wuhu. The old embankment on the riverside is as dilapidated as the Xijiang embankment. However, the new embankment is more solid, and both sides are paved with square stone slabs, which is very suitable for automobile roads. Director Xi Dejiong of the Engineering Relief Department said that it is planned to plant willows on the side facing the river in the future, which will not only be spectacular but also protect the embankment. He hopes that it can be realized as soon as possible. At 12:00 PM, they returned to the main ship for lunch.

(Huangsitan Dike Project) At 2:30 PM in the afternoon, they took a small boat to Huangsitan Wuxian Dike in Wuwei County on the north bank. Gao Hengshou, the magistrate of Wuhu County, accompanied them in person and sent a platoon of soldiers to protect them. It is said that although large groups of bandits have disappeared in the area, small groups still appear from time to time, so it is necessary to be cautious. The Huangsitan Dike Project is related to the lives and property of seven counties in northern Anhui, so it is very important. The old dike is semi-circular, and the new dike has been changed to a straight line. Wuwei County is the area with the most rice and grain. Although there was a good harvest this year after last year's disaster, they are only able to make a living because the grain is cheap. The villagers lamented their poverty and complained to the delegation members, and some even knelt on the ground and begged for relief. The people's livelihood is like this, which is very sad. According to Magistrate Gao, the Huangsitan Dike Project is subject to the attack of the river water on the riverside. Every three years, the old dike must be submerged, and a new dike must be rebuilt. The farmland in the nearby area has been completely abandoned due to the intrusion of river sand. Therefore, if we want to protect the dike, we must first dredge the river, and the protection of the dike itself is secondary. The new Huangsitan dike can be maintained for up to 15 years after it is straightened. However, the local authorities must pay attention to it at all times. There is a Wuxian Temple on the old dike, which is commonly known as the Wutong Temple. There are still a small number of thatched huts on the new dike. Zhou Xiangxian, the chairman of the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission, told Gao personally to enact laws to force them to move, otherwise it would be even more difficult to do so after a long time. It is not only unsightly but also hinders traffic. Magistrate Gao agreed. The inspection ended and they returned to the ship at 4:00 PM. Because it was late, the inspection of Daijialongtan on the north bank was cancelled. According to the engineers, Daijialongtan has a lower terrain, so the dike is very high, reaching several zhang. It is conceivable that the project is great, and it is the most important in the second district's project. At 5:00 PM, the Jiangxin ship set sail from Wuhu and arrived at Datong at 10:00 PM.

(Procedure on the 30th) The inspection procedure on the 30th is scheduled as follows: After breakfast at 7:00 AM on the 30th, at 9:00 AM, they will land at Datong Yangyouzhan to inspect the dike project on the south bank, which belongs to Section 9 of the third district. At 10:00 AM, they will return to Jiangxin and sail to Saozhougou to inspect Section 7 of the third district. At 12:30 PM, they will return to Jiangxin for lunch and sail upstream. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, they will take a small sampan to Zongyang Town to inspect the Guangji Embankment, a famous dike project in Anhui. At 4:00 PM, they will arrive at Majia to inspect the breach and the rebuilt new dike. At 5:00 PM, they will arrive at Anqing for a tea party hosted by the Anhui Provincial Government. After the procedure was decided, some people suggested that they should first inspect the unfinished dike project at Liubai Zhang to observe the dike-building situation on the ground. Therefore, the plan was changed. At 8:00 AM on the 30th, they first took a small boat to the Liubai Zhang area in Tongcheng County on the north bank, which still belongs to the second district's project.

(A Glimpse of Dike Building) At 7:30 AM on the 30th, the Anhui Provincial Government sent the Anping small boat to welcome them, and Chairman Wu Zhongxin sent a letter to Chu Minyi expressing his welcome. The entire group then took the Anping boat and sailed down to the vicinity of the Huihe River on the north bank to inspect the Liubai Zhang dike project. This section has not yet been completed and is currently being rushed to completion by more than 3,000 workers. The area is a place where bandits appear, so dozens of soldiers were sent in advance to protect them. When the entire group landed, more than 20 military police in the boat also went along to prevent accidents. It is said that on the evening of the 29th, several local gentry in Datong went to the area to welcome them. Because it was late at night, the garrison saw that their behavior was suspicious and opened fire. One person was grazed by a bullet on the nose and suffered a minor injury. It is conceivable that the situation is serious, so today the members of the delegation were cautious when they landed and moved forward. Reeds grow luxuriantly along the way, as dense as forests, about a zhang high, which is a great barrier for bandits. The villagers build giant sheds with reeds as dwellings. The area is famous for producing reeds, which can be sold for 40,000 to 50,000 yuan a year. It is about four or five li from the riverside to the new dike. Lu Guan walked, and the guards in front were scattered to release sentries, and reached the new dike after twists and turns. The work of building the dike was in full swing at that time. More than 3,000 workers were working separately, pulling soil, carrying mud, and building the dike, each doing their own thing. Most of the workers were transported from northern Anhui, and very few natives were employed, as most of them had returned to their own agricultural work. According to Mr. Xi Dejiong, the flood relief dike project does not have a contracting system. Twenty-five people are placed in a shed with a foreman to supervise them. Twenty-four people go out to work, and another person specializes in food and other chores in the shed, so the order is well-organized. However, the new dike area above Hankou is a nest of bandits. No one responded to the recruitment of workers, so military labor had to be used before it could be built. It is also said that this section of the project was not within the planned project of the flood relief association. Due to the repeated invitations of local people, they had to reluctantly do their best. Now that the flood relief association has ended, the dike project has been transferred to the National Economic Council for management. They returned to the small boat at 11:00 AM and returned to the main boat for lunch at 12:00 PM. The inspection of the second district project ended at this point (Qian Hua from Anqing, November 30).

The National Government's Flood Relief Committee received a telegram from Jiujiang the day before yesterday, stating that the delegation had completed its inspection in Fogan Zhou, Guadong, Yijishan, Lugang, Huangsitan, Liubai Zhang, Guangji Embankment, Mahua Dike, Huikou, Duanyao, and other places. The committee members expressed their satisfaction with the achievements of the dike repair projects in various places. Director Xi Dejiong of the Engineering Relief Department is still accompanying the committee members to continue to inspect upstream, and is expected to arrive in Xun this day (1st).

Preservation of Accumulated Grain and Property in Municipal and County Areas

Provincial Government's Order

Regarding the Shanghai County's original accumulated grain and property division between the municipality and county, the matter has not yet been implemented. Now, the county government states that since the division of the municipality and county, the original accumulated grain and property of the county have been jointly managed by both parties. Any use of funds requires mutual consent, which has greatly hindered preparations for famine relief and the progress of essential policies. As the county government is about to relocate, it has submitted a report to the province and municipality, requesting a prompt decision on the division to clarify boundaries and facilitate implementation. However, the Municipal Bureau of Finance has convened several meetings to assess the value of immovable property and decided on a public auction for division. Subsequently, Shanghai citizens such as Yao Wen-nan submitted reports to the province and county, stating that the accumulated grain and property were donated by the people for famine relief and were related to the people's livelihood, requesting a halt to the auction. It is reported that after receiving the reports, the provincial government has already consulted the Shanghai Municipal Government for investigation and instructed the Shanghai County Government accordingly.

Donations to the Northeast Volunteer Army - Yesterday's Report

The Northeast Volunteer Army Relief Association received notifications from various donation collection points yesterday, as well as the number of military uniforms received. Details are listed separately below. Huang Chu-jiu's Movable Property to Be Auctioned Without Price Limit

All movable property in Huang Chu-jiu's former residence at 914 Avenue Edward VII, known as Zhi-zu-lu, is being auctioned by the Da Hua Auction Company. Due to excessively high price limits, few people are buying. It has been learned that the court has already approved this. The auction is scheduled for December 5th, 6th, and 7th, starting at 2:30 PM each day at Zhi-zu-lu. Those who wish to purchase these bargains can visit on the 3rd and 4th to view them and participate in the auction at the appointed time. Don't miss this opportunity.

Abundant in Both Firearms and Money, Crimes Committed Are All Cases of Kidnapping for Ransom

The Notorious Bandit Chen Zhao-qi and His Gang Have Considerable Skill

The Police Are Currently Investigating

Possessing a Machine Gun That Can Fire Fifty Rounds Continuously

And 1,369 Bullets

Also Possessing a Large Sum Savings Passbook from Sincere Company

Chief Detective You A-gen and Detective Zhou Gui-sen of the Old Gate Police Station apprehended eight individuals, including the notorious bandit Chen Zhao-qi (also known as Ni Si) from Shao-xing, Yuan Guang-yao, Yuan Dian-lai, Ma Zheng-cai, Lu Zeng-gong, and women Chen Hu-shi, Yuan Wang-shi, Chen San-feng, and Jin Wang-shi, one after another in places such as East Yu-heng Road on the previous day. They confiscated one submachine gun, which can fire fifty rounds continuously, 1,369 bullets, cash amounting to 1,342.50 yuan, a savings book from Sincere Company with approximately six to seven thousand yuan, five gold rings, one gold watch, one gold bracelet, and one gold lock pendant. All items were taken back to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special Court's Criminal Division One, where Criminal Judge Qian Hong-ye presided over the interrogation. The police lawyer, Ru Bao-yi, stated that the cases committed by the defendants were all major cases of kidnapping for ransom, but the police were currently conducting investigations to apprehend accomplices, and the details of the crimes had not yet been thoroughly investigated. Therefore, he requested permission to detain them for further investigation. Judge Qian approved the lawyer Ru's request and ordered the defendants to be returned to custody separately for another hearing in one week.

Robbers are Extremely Wicked, Committing Both Adultery and Theft

Only One Person Among the Twelve Was Uninvolved

The Victim's Cousin Was the Real Culprit

On the morning of the 23rd of last month, at approximately 1:00 AM, nine bandits, including the notorious bandits Xu Shu-ming from Li-yang and Zhao Wen-shi and Dong Yong-fa from Jiang-bei, led a gang armed with Russian weapons to rob Liang Xue-fu, a Dan-ning resident living in a thatched shed in Shen-jia-tan, Yang-pu, taking jewelry, clothing, and silver worth over two hundred yuan. The two bandits, Zhao and Dong, also took turns raping Liang Xue-fu's nineteen-year-old younger sister, Liang Xiao-mei, before fleeing. The case was investigated and the perpetrators were apprehended by Hua Detective Lu Gen-sheng and Yang Pei-sheng, and Detectives Li Peng-fei of the Yu-lin Road Police Station one after another, along with the woman Chen Xu-shi, the receiver of stolen goods Zhu Guo-rui, and the suspect Xu De-you. All were escorted to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Lin-yu presided over the hearing in Court Three. The police lawyer, Zhang Tian-yin, stated that the doctor's examination of Liang Xiao-mei revealed that she was not a virgin, so the rape aspect of the case would not be investigated. Today, they all arrived in court and presented some of the original stolen clothes, a wooden clock, and a medical certificate for inspection. The court ordered separate interrogations of each defendant and ordered those not involved in the case to leave the courtroom. According to the victim, Liang Xue-fu, Liang Xue-wen among the defendants was his cousin, living across from his house (i.e., the instigator of the crime). At 11:00 PM, the robbers broke in, approximately five or six people, threatening silence. The five members of his family were awakened from their dreams. The robbers did not allow them to get up. He saw one robber holding an iron rod and another raping his sister on her bed. His sister cried out slightly, then there was no sound. They were robbed of forty yuan in cash, one gold ring, and more than twenty pieces of clothing. Afterwards, his cousin, Liang Xue-wen, said that the robbers who committed the robbery were probably from the Pu-ai-fang neighborhood on Yang-shu-pu Road, and that he had no prior grudges against them. According to his brother, Liang Xue-fa, at the time, the robbers pressed down on his head so that he could not sit up, threatening to shoot him if he did. According to Liang Xue-fu's wife, Ms. Yin, at that time, her husband and sister were crying hysterically on the bed, then there was no sound. According to the girl, Liang Xiao-mei, nineteen years old, already betrothed to someone, one robber climbed onto her bed, pressed her down, took off her velvet shirt, jacket, and trousers, stuffed her mouth with the velvet shirt, preventing her from making any noise, and raped her. Afterwards, he took the velvet shirt and fled. A moment later, another robber came, snatched her trousers, held a small knife, and forced her to submit to rape. After finishing, he got off the bed. The court ordered the defendant Xu Shu-ming to testify. His cousin Xu Huai-zhen (i.e., the second defendant) and the defendant Wu Yun-sheng’s son accompanied him but did not enter. Wu gave him a wooden clock and asked him to leave it at his daughter Chen Xu-shi’s place. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Xu Huai-zhen and Wu Yun-sheng’s son testified that Little Jiang-bei went to rob. Zhao Wen-bao testified that he knew Xu Shu-ming and saw the girl Liang Xiao-mei sleeping in bed when he entered the victim’s home, sending her off to have intercourse. When she tried to make noise, he threatened her into silence. Afterwards, he did not rob any property. Lu Li-zhi testified that he knew the defendant Zhu Guo-rui but did not go to rob at the time because he was sick at home. Later, Little Jiang-bei asked him to sell some stolen clothes for them. Dong Yong-hong testified that Little Jiang-bei invited him to rob and that he raped Liang Xiao-mei. He did not use a knife to threaten her. Fei Shao-yu testified that Little Jiang-bei invited him to play and did not say that he was going to rob. Liang Xue-wen testified that he had previously mentioned to Wang Xue-li that his cousin Liang Xue-fu's family had money, which Little Jiang-bei overheard, and this caused the disaster. Wang Xue-li testified that he and Liang Xue-wen had previously complained about their hardships, and Lu Li-zhi was also present, but he did not go to rob. Chen Xu-shi testified that her father Xu Shu-ming gave her a wooden clock. When the police detectives arrived, they arrested her father. She hid the clock in the yellow sand, but it was still found. Zhu Guo-rui testified that he knew Lu Li-zhi and that on the 23rd of last month, he sold him three pieces of clothing for two yuan, and he did not know that they were stolen. He asked for judgment. The police lawyer Zhang stated that the police had determined that the twenty-second defendant, Xu De-you, was not involved and requested that he be released. Judge Zhao ordered the other eleven defendants to be returned to custody separately for another hearing and approved the release of Xu De-you.

Bandit Commits Suicide Out of Fear of Punishment

Using a Chopstick to Stab into His Head

Then Violently Slamming Himself Against the Wall

| His Death Was Indeed Tragic |

The kidnapping bandit Wu Hong-cheng, from Jiang-bei, twenty-seven years old, kidnapped Wu Tong-chao in his hometown on March 12th of this year, demanding a ransom of 1,500 yuan, to be negotiated in Shanghai. On September 13th, the bandit encountered Wu Shen-shi, the daughter-in-law of the hostage, on Avenue Edward VII, and she reported him to the police, who dispatched detectives to arrest Wu and take him to the Xin-zha Police Station. After being interrogated by the First Special District Court, he was ordered to be escorted in for further questioning. The morning before, he was again escorted to the court for further questioning. Judge Wu Zhen presided over the hearing in Criminal Court Two, questioning the bandit once before he was taken back to the police station to be temporarily detained by the police. The previous evening at approximately 9:00 PM, Wu Zhen-xiang, a staff member from the Jiangsu Security Department, arrived with documents to escort him. He arrived at the detention center with the deputy chief Tuile and was about to bring the prisoner out and hand him over to the visiting staff when the prisoner heard the news. He immediately took out a bamboo chopstick that he had hidden beforehand and stabbed it into his own head, violently slamming himself against the wall, causing it to penetrate several inches. He bled profusely and immediately fell to the ground. The police officers immediately sent him to the hospital for treatment, but he died due to his injuries.

The body was transported to the autopsy center on Pei-lun Road. Yesterday morning, Zhang Yao-guang, a prosecutor from the First Special Court, and Wang Zu-yi, a forensic clerk, were commissioned to go to the center to examine the body, and the case was officially recorded. According to deputy chief Tuile, when he and the staff member arrived at the detention center, as soon as they called out Wu Hong-cheng's name, he stabbed himself with a chopstick, and they were unable to rescue him. Another prisoner, Xu Run-feng, and Xi Qing-lin, who lived in the same cell, also testified to this. Zhang then declared that the deceased, Wu Hong-cheng, a male and a criminal, had indeed died from a chopstick wound to the head. The body was handed over to Pu-shan Villa for encoffining, and the chopstick was kept on file.

Car and Smuggling

Inconsistencies in the Chauffeur's Statements

Lu Rong-gao's Presence in Hangzhou and Shanghai is Suspicious

Lu Rong-gao (also known as Lu Lao-san and Lu A-san), from Jiang-bei, operated the Jiu-jiang Automobile Company at numbers 279 Jiu-jiang Road and 902 Wei-hai-wei Road. At 6:40 PM on the 24th of last month, car number 17531 from the company was stolen in the Mo-hua Street area. The chauffeur, Li A-si, from Zhen-jiang, reported the theft to the Old Gate Police Station, requesting an investigation. The police chief issued an order to all road stations and Chinese and Western police officers to be vigilant and to detain the car immediately if found. Unexpectedly, at 8:20 PM on the same day, Indian Constable number 351, stationed at the intersection of Long-men Road and Da-gu Road, saw car number 17531 traveling west. He immediately ordered the car to stop and saw that there was a chauffeur and another man in the car. The Indian constable jumped onto the car and ordered them to drive to the Old Gate Police Station. When the car reached the entrance of the Tianchan Theater at the intersection of Yun-nan Road and Fu-zhou Road, the other man suddenly ordered the chauffeur to stop, opened the door, and fled into the Tianchan Theater. As the Indian constable had to guard the chauffeur and the car, he could not pursue him and had to let him escape. He then escorted the chauffeur to the police station, where detectives Wang Jin-shou and Bao Cui-lou questioned him. The chauffeur identified himself as Gao Chang-sheng from Zhen-jiang. When asked why he was driving the car, he said that he used to be a chauffeur but was now unemployed. On the 23rd, he met a man surnamed Ma in a gambling den in the French Concession. Ma told him that Lu Lao-san, the head of Jiu-jiang, wanted to transport a large quantity of opium and needed to find a driver. Ma asked Gao if he could take on this task and said he would be rewarded in the future. Gao agreed because he had been unemployed for a long time. On the 24th, Ma led him to the entrance of the Tianchan Theater and told him to wait outside while he went inside. Shortly after, Ma came out and told him to wait at the intersection of Min-guo Road at Xin-bei-men. Gao went as agreed, and Ma and Lu Lao-san were already there, and the car was also parked there. Lu gave him six sheets of black paper and a box of paste and said that if anyone discovered them transporting the opium, they should paste the black paper over the license plates. Then, Gao drove the car to Long-men Road to prepare to transport the opium but was arrested by the police. After obtaining this statement, the detectives went to the two car companies on Jiu-jiang Road and Wei-hai-wei Road to arrest Lu Rong-gao, but he was nowhere to be found. They only confiscated three small photographs of Lu and brought them back to the police station. Gao Chang-sheng identified the photographs as Lu Lao-san without a doubt. The detectives also detained Li A-si, believing that he might be involved as an accomplice, and sent him to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. On that day, Lu suddenly went to the Old Gate Police Station with lawyer Wu *Kun. The detectives detained Lu, and Gao identified him again. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Court One of the First Special Court. The police lawyer Ru Bao-yi explained the case and said that Gao and Lu were being prosecuted under Articles 6 and 12 of the Opium Suppression Act. Li A-si was not being prosecuted but would be a witness. Lu Le-gao denied this at the police station, saying that he had gone to Hangzhou on the 22nd of last month and returned to Shanghai on the 29th, but the times he gave for the train departure did not match. It should be investigated. Gao Chang-sheng suddenly said that he could not identify Lu with certainty, but the rest of his statement was largely the same as the police's statement. Lu hired lawyer Fan Gang, and Lu hired lawyer Wu Lin-kun to defend him. Judge Qian Hong-ye said that further investigation was needed and ordered that the hearing be postponed and the defendants be returned to custody.

Breach of Contract Dispute Over a Chartered Ship

Asia Eastern Sues Tongyu for Four Counts

Seeking Compensation of 76,000 Yuan

Asia Eastern Shipping Company chartered the newly built Ping'an steamship from Beijing Road Tongyu Shipping Company in October of last year. A lease was signed for a period of four months, with a monthly rent of 8,000 yuan. The terms within the agreement were extremely detailed and stipulated that in the event of war affecting the shipping routes, both parties could terminate the contract. After signing, Asia Eastern Company entered into a contract with Huai River salt merchants to transport salt using the ship. However, Tongyu Company initially failed to deliver the ship as agreed, then prohibited the loading and unloading of goods, and finally, before the expiration of the term, abruptly repossessed the ship. These irregular actions caused Asia Eastern significant losses. Now, its manager, Mo Zhaoyun, has retained lawyers Yang Linzhi, Zhang Jiahui, and Ye Shaoying to file a lawsuit for damages against Tongyu Company's manager, Zheng Xitang, listing four counts: (A) Article 32 of the lease stipulates that the defendant should deliver the vessel within the period from November 20th to December 10th of the 20th year to provide transportation for the plaintiff. However, after contracting with the plaintiff, the defendant entered into another charter agreement with a third party, and around December 10th, sailed the ship to Andong to transport goods to Dalian, and then to Hong Kong, earning freight of 23,475 yuan. During this time, the salt transportation contract made by the plaintiff suffered losses of 35,000 yuan due to salt accumulation and spoilage. The defendant only delivered the ship on December 24th, a delay of 14 days. In addition to the 35,000 yuan loss due to the delay in salt transportation, the actual daily loss was 400 yuan, totaling 5,600 yuan for 14 days, bringing the total loss to 40,600 yuan. (B) After the defendant delivered the ship to the plaintiff on December 24th, the plaintiff immediately paid one month's rent and ordered the ship to sail to Haizhou to transport salt. When the January 28th Incident occurred, businesses closed, banks suspended operations, and remittances were impossible, making it impossible to pay the second installment of rent. This force majeure event was not attributable to the plaintiff. Commercial practices encourage mutual understanding, and the law provides for exemption from payment. However, the defendant used this as a pretext to take matters into its own hands, prohibiting the loading and unloading of goods, causing the ship to be docked in Jiujiang and unable to operate. On February 10th of this year, the defendant demanded a postdated check for 4,000 yuan as a condition for unloading the cargo, agreeing that the check would be honored after the cargo was unloaded. However, after receiving the check, the defendant did not fulfill the unloading. Therefore, the plaintiff had to stop payment. On March 10th, the defendant again stated that it was willing to exchange the previous overdue check for a newly issued check for 5,500 yuan, promising to telegraph the ship owner to open the hatch and unload the cargo. However, after the plaintiff prepared payment, the defendant not only failed to return the old check but also continued to refuse to release the cargo, as evidenced by the defendant's telegram to the ship owner on February 25th. In total, the defendant detained the ship for 66 days, resulting in a loss of 26,400 yuan at a rate of 400 yuan per day. (C) During the term of the contract, the ship should be operated by the plaintiff. Without the plaintiff's permission, the defendant had no right to direct its operation. However, in April of this year, the defendant's Yuanda steamship ran aground in Huangzhou. Without consulting the plaintiff, the defendant arbitrarily unloaded and stored the salt from the Xinping steamship in Xunyang and withheld the plaintiff's salt warehouse receipt for 1,000 yuan. The ship was then sailed to Huangzhou for towing for several days, resulting in a business loss of over 7,000 yuan to the plaintiff. (D) The contract stipulated a term of four months from the date of delivery of the ship. Since the defendant delivered the ship on December 24th of the 20th year, the contract should have expired on April 24th of this year. However, when the ship arrived in Shanghai on April 19th, the defendant unilaterally repossessed the ship before the contract expired, causing a loss of 2,000 yuan to the plaintiff. Therefore, it should be ordered that the defendant compensate the plaintiff 76,000 yuan and bear the litigation costs. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang of the First Special District Court held a hearing. The defendant also retained lawyer Zhao Sheng to defend. Plaintiff's lawyers Yang Linzhi and others stated the intent of the lawsuit and presented evidence such as the contract. After the defendant's lawyer responded, Judge Yang adjourned the hearing for a later date.

Unprecedented and Unparalleled Grand Amusement

Initiated by Three Organizations…Righteous in Name

Boy Scouts Selling Tickets…Purchase as Much as Possible

Storytellers, Theater Box Offices, and Movie Stars Included

Teams, Musical Bands, and Famous Beijing Opera Performers Participating

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, General Labor Union, Lawyers Association, and Accountants Association have specially launched a grand amusement event to help the Northeastern refugees. It will be held at the New World starting on the 15th of this month. All proceeds from ticket sales will be used to relieve Northeastern refugees.

Ticket Sales Situation: It is heard that the association’s amusement tickets have already been printed. Boy Scouts from the city are going door-to-door to promote sales. Citizens are actively purchasing tickets. Even foreign friends in Shanghai are actively buying tickets because it concerns a righteous cause. Therefore, the results of ticket sales have been very good in recent days. Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce was afraid that a few shops were not clear, so it issued another notice to all industries to purchase as much as possible.

Chamber of Commerce Announcement: Sirs, for the purpose of rescuing Northeastern refugees, this association is jointly launching the Relief Northeast Refugee Amusement Fair with the General Labor Union, Lawyers Association, and Accountants Association. Starting today, the Boy Scouts of this association will be assigned to sell tickets door-to-door, and they will carry the certificate issued by this association for credibility. Each association should immediately issue an urgent notice to inform its members to purchase as much as possible when the Boy Scouts come to sell tickets, in order to help save the country and the Northeast. Do not shirk and delay matters. This is extremely important. Respectfully announced, and Xiang Gong Sui.

Resolution of Trademark Dispute Between Family and South China

Trademark Bureau Orders Cancellation of Butterfly Brand

The Family Industrial Society and the South China Arts and Crafts Society previously had a dispute over the imitation of the Invincible brand and the Butterfly brand, which has not been resolved. Yesterday, it was learned that the National Trademark Bureau paid close attention to this matter. After a long period of research, the Bureau determined that the Butterfly brand had a clear suspicion of imitating the Invincible brand and has ordered the South China Arts and Crafts Society to cancel it. The reason is that although the names "Invincible" and "Butterfly" are different in characters, they sound the same, especially in Shanghai, where the pronunciation is not easy to distinguish. Furthermore, although the "Butterfly" brand uses the image of a butterfly as a pattern, it also has the pattern of a butterfly and the English word "Butterfly." The "Invincible" brand trademark has been used by the Family Industrial Society for nearly 20 years and has been registered for a patent. Therefore, in order to protect the rights and interests of the Family Industrial Society, the Trademark Bureau ordered the South China Arts and Crafts Society to cancel it voluntarily.

International Propaganda Society Welcomes Overseas Chinese Leader Lin Yishun

The China International Propaganda Society was founded in the aftermath of the January 28th Anti-Japanese War. Since its establishment, the society has published major works such as "The Course of the Songhu Bloody Battle" and "The War Clouds Between the United States and Japan," which have been widely supported by the public. Overseas Chinese comrades in Nanyang have also strongly supported all the society's activities. Mr. Lin Yishun is a revolutionary predecessor of the overseas Chinese in Nanyang and is happy to assist in various domestic undertakings. This time, he returned to Shanghai from the Northwest and South. He believes that international propaganda is an important strategy for saving the country today and is particularly enthusiastic in advocating and supporting it. The society held a special welcome for Mr. Lin at the Dongya Restaurant last night, and invited dignitaries from all walks of life such as Tang Hai'an and Wen Hongen to accompany him as guests. The hosts and guests had a joyful time until 11 o'clock.

There is No Shortage of Raw Materials for Domestically Produced Parasols

The Shanghai Umbrella Trade Association sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, saying: "Respectfully, today's local news in your newspaper carried a story about overseas Chinese who returned to the country to establish an umbrella raw material factory. The draft mentioned that our country has never produced umbrella raw materials. They are all imported and the annual leakage is huge." This statement does not match the facts. This association is a group of umbrella industry members. Umbrella factories and raw material factories all join as members. Currently, umbrella raw material factories include Huali, Renhe, Samsung Hexin, Xin Dacheng, Li Yuanxing, Xue Linji, Tang Fuxing, etc., all of which cooperate in division of labor. Their products are sufficient for umbrella factories to use. Only a very small number of high-end products come from overseas. Therefore, this special letter requests immediate correction to reveal the facts."

Gan Azhen Brutally Hacked with an Ax, Spine Broken

Formerly a Detective in the Public Security Bureau

No Changes Expected Within Seven Days

Gan Azhen, formerly a detective in the Public Security Bureau, from Ningbo, lived in Shengan Lane, Zixia Road, Nanshi. The day before yesterday afternoon, he went out from his home and walked to Zhujia Lane, a very secluded place. Suddenly, five or six enemies approached him from behind and hacked him with a sharp ax. His spine was broken, and his head and arms were cut in seven or eight places. He fell to the ground, unconscious. The murderers, seeing that their goal had been achieved, fled. Later, his family members were informed and arrived at the scene, finding him lying in a pool of blood. He did not respond to their questions. They immediately took him to the Nanshi Hospital for treatment. Because his spine was injured internally, he was transferred to the Beishi Bone Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, three of his spinal bones were broken, and the internal injuries were also very serious. If there are no changes within a week, his life can be saved without any problems, but he will not be fully recovered for a while. It may take one or two months to recover and be discharged from the hospital.

Hu Jinshui Finds it Difficult to Please Both Sides

Wu Shanwen Sued in Criminal Court

Hu Jinshui, from Huizhou, lived at No. 495 Yuanfang Road, Gangkou. He was working as an account splitting runner at Xiangmao Paint Shop on Changsha Road, Xinzha Road. In April of this year, Wu Shanwen, the manager of Xiangmao and a fellow villager, resigned and opened his own Dayou Paint Shop on Dewatt Road, West China Road. Wu needed a runner and repeatedly asked Hu to resign from Xiangmao and transfer to his shop as a runner, offering a monthly salary of 20 yuan plus a 7-yuan transportation allowance. Hu, seeing that the salary was better than at Xiangmao, accepted the job as a runner in Wu's shop. Unexpectedly, Hu suddenly fell ill, and Wu ignored him. His friend sent him to Huining Hospital for treatment. When he recovered and returned to the shop, Wu suddenly terminated his employment and did not pay his salary as agreed. According to Hu, while he was in the hospital for treatment, Wu even opened his suitcase without permission and took several pieces of clothing, pawning them. Hu was in a dilemma, so he requested a judgment from the Paint Industry Association and the Bureau of Social Affairs. Unexpectedly, Wu suddenly claimed that Hu had taken a bucket of Tulip brand lead powder worth 73 taels from the Catholic Church Weichengzhi Paint and Pigment Shop in the French Concession in August of last year, and that the money had been paid by him on his behalf. He hired a lawyer to request mediation from the First Special Court, claiming creditor's rights. When the court held a mediation hearing, Hu completely denied this, saying that the Chengzhi's bill of presentation was forged by Wu. Therefore, the mediation failed. However, Hu believed that Wu had forged an account and fabricated facts to deceive the court into requesting mediation, which greatly damaged his personal reputation. Therefore, he hired lawyer Chen Jia'yin to file a criminal self-accusation against Wu Shanwen in the First Special Court. The trial was held in the Eighth Court yesterday. After a debate by lawyers on both sides, the court ordered that Sun, the runner from Chengzhi Shop, and Wu Songhua, the owner of Xiangmao Shop, be summoned on the 13th of this month for questioning and verification.

Mr. Liu Tingfang's Letter, December 2, 1932

Recently, I came to Shanghai for some business, and I happened to learn that your newspaper is taking advantage of its 60th anniversary celebration to re-establish its working policy with the spirit of self-improvement and to intensify its efforts. This is truly a delightful thing that is enough to make people feel refreshed. I eagerly awaited December 1st, and as soon as the morning came, I bought a copy of your newspaper. When I opened it, I saw that the layout was clearer, the "Free Talk" section had been reformed, and there were new features such as the "Circulating Library Amateur Weekly" and "Reader Advisors." A whole string of good news was presented before my eyes. A new vitality and dynamism were active on every page. I couldn't help but exclaim: "Shen Bao is not old!"

Because of my deep love for it, I also have high expectations. Here, I have some opinions regarding the "Reader Advisors" section, and I would like to express them.

According to the introduction of the "Reader Advisors": "...this newspaper will select several experts to provide answers to questions raised by the readers," but in the brief rules, it is also noted that the scope of the questions is limited to eight items such as politics and economics. What I want to offer for your newspaper's reference are these two points.

First, I feel that there is no need to limit the questions that are raised. Because the universe is so vast, and everything before our eyes is a question. Which question should be discussed and which question should not be discussed? Since your newspaper is willing to be a consultant to the readers, it does not seem appropriate to impose such a limitation on the readers. I believe that every question has value for discussion, from the heavens to the earth, from ancient reptiles to dust. There is nothing that cannot be discussed. Why put up an annoying fence in this lively garden?

Second, the introduction also says: "All problems and difficulties are not personal." This statement is absolutely correct. Precisely because the problems are not personal, I suggest that the responsibility for answering questions should not be solely borne by your few (experts). It is best to have all the readers freely offer their opinions for lively discussion (of course, this refers to some major issues). Then, your (advisors) can summarize the opinions and draw a conclusion. In this way, on the one hand, you can "draw on collective wisdom," and on the other hand, you can prevent the "Reader Advisors" from becoming like a collection of answers to three hundred difficult arithmetic problems. Moreover, there is no guarantee that these difficult problems can be completely solved.

That is my humble opinion. What do you gentlemen think?

X X X X

Reporter's Note: Mr. Liu is currently a professor at Peking University and Yenching University and is one of the leading scholars in our country. We believe that the two points he raised regarding this column are of great value and should be fully accepted, and we express our gratitude. In the future, readers can feel free to raise questions, but our brief rules do not need to be modified in terms of wording. As for the second point, we will fully adopt Mr. Liu's opinion. Except for some trivial issues, for other more important ones, we will not answer them first. We will only publish the original letter and submit it for public discussion. After a certain stage of discussion, we will then synthesize the opinions and draw a conclusion.

Here is a question for the public to start discussing:

X X X X

Ms. Zhang Yunqiu's Letter, December 1, 1932

Here is a question that may seem unimportant but is actually very important, and perhaps you gentlemen have already felt it.

A couple, from falling in love to getting married, this stage is usually full of sweetness and satisfaction, with the feeling of "wishing to be mandarin ducks and not envying the immortals" or "wishing to be buried in the same coffin after death." But once the honeymoon is over, the feelings of the new couple have already dropped from "so strong that they cannot be melted" to "can be melted." After another month or two, after another year or two, they gradually feel that there is only obligation between them, and no feelings. Then, they begin to get angry with each other, then they start to use harsh words, and finally, quarrels arise from time to time. The man sighs, and the woman also frowns. Further, unfortunate things are staged. Tragedies like this are everywhere, and I am unfortunately one of the leading actors in this tragedy.

Sir, I want to ask you: (1) Why do countless couples fall from the boiling point of love to zero degrees? (2) What methods can be used to remedy such a tragedy? Dear Sir, I hope you can answer this difficult question for me.

The Huacheng Tobacco Company's Solicitation of Cigarette Trademark Names and Designs Has Ended

The Huacheng Tobacco Company previously advertised for cigarette trademark names and designs. In addition to the most submissions from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, submissions were also received from as far away as Shaanxi, Sichuan, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Guangdong. A total of more than 8,000 entries were received. The company specially invited trademark experts and literary giants Yan Duhe, Wang Yingbin, Dong XianGuang, Zhou Shoujuan, Ma Yinliang, Pan Gongbi, Xiong Shaohao, and Zeng Xubai to judge at the Central Vegetable Agency on Sima Road the other night. In order to ensure careful selection, the company first asked Shen Weiting of the Chinese Tobacco Factory Trade Association and Chen Liangyu of the Tobacco Exchange Trade Association to review the entries. Any names that were the same or similar to those of other tobacco company products were immediately rejected. There were also names such as Fugui, Sanyou, Tianzhen, Fenfang, and Fada. The company already had products with these names for sale and, according to the solicitation rules, they were rejected. The results of the review and judgment are detailed on the cover of today's newspaper and will not be repeated here.

New Book and Newspaper News

Publication of "Chinese Architecture": The first issue of "Chinese Architecture," published by the Chinese Architectural Society, was published yesterday. The main contents include Zhao Shen's inaugural speech, Fan Wenzhao's history of the Chinese Architectural Society, Dong Dayou's Shanghai Municipal Government Housing Design Report, Tong Jun's Two Pagoda Temples in Beiping, Liang Huicheng's congratulations to the first graduating class of the Department of Architecture of Northeastern University, Wang Jin's Soviet Government New Star Architecture, Shanghai Public Concession Housing Construction Regulations translated by Shang Wang, and the History of the Department of Architecture of the Northeastern University China Building at next year's Chicago Exposition. There is also a four-color plate of the new building of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau and more than 30 other photos. The entire book is printed on 120-pound glossy paper. One issue is published monthly, with 12 issues per year. The subscription office is located at Room 407, 4th Floor, Mainland Shopping Center, Nanjing Road, Shanghai.

The Second Issue of "Research on China's Way Out" Published: Edited by Wang Yishan, "Research on China's Way Out" has been well-received by readers since its publication. The first issue has already sold out and will be reprinted soon. The second issue has now been published. The main contents are as follows: The emergence and development of international parties, the way out for diplomacy with Japan, the world economic panic and the world economic conference, the transformation of the international situation and the contradictions of Japanese diplomacy, the shifting Chinese politics, the internationalization of Fascism and China, and Stalin's "Problems of Leninism" (translated and published periodically). The general distributor is the Taidong Bookstore at 124-5 Sima Road. The retail price is 20 cents per issue, and the subscription price is one yuan for half a year and two yuan for a full year.

"Chunqiu" Published Today: "Chunqiu Weekly," run by Cui Tongyue, Li Yiwei, and others, was published today. The editors Huang Shuanghua, Chen Zuduan, and Chen Zhitian are all able to write truthfully and deeply in accordance with the original meaning of "Chunqiu." It is said that their background is the "National Weekly," which was once famous for its bold and daring speech. Now it is named "Chunqiu."

Fire on Yichang Road

Fire at Dayou Factory Workshop on Yichang Road, Shanghai West: Yesterday afternoon at 3:15, a fire broke out unexpectedly. The flames soared, and the fire was uncontrollable. In a short time, two workshops were burned down. Later, the fire brigade rushed to the scene and tried their best to put out the fire. It was not until a while later that the fire was extinguished.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory reported at 4:30 PM yesterday: The weather around Shandong is expected to have northeasterly winds. The coastal area south of Ma'anshan Island and the Yangtze River basin are expected to become gradually cloudy, with fog or drizzle and easterly winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 66.3 degrees and the lowest was 44.6 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 57.4 degrees and the lowest was 52.3 degrees.

Shanghai Northeastern Refugee Relief Association

Monthly Donation Campaign

Urgent Announcement

More than a year has passed since the fall of the Northeast. The whole country is silent, relying only on the righteous army to fight desperately. The dead are lying in corpses in the borderlands, and the living are fighting in blood. If we do not expand rescue and provide long-term assistance, the righteous army will be destroyed and the Northeast will be lost, and China will also be lost. Therefore, based on the principle of saving people and saving ourselves, we have jointly discussed the monthly donation method.

(1) This monthly donation is limited to six months. (2) The Northeastern Refugee Relief Association is established in Beiping as the central organization for relief in the Northeast, chaired by General Zhu Ziqiao. All donations from this association will be remitted to the association for distribution. (3) All office expenses will be borne by the initiators, and no donation funds will be used at all. (4) Receiving agencies: 1. Major banks in Shanghai 2. Hengxun, Fuyuan, Tongchun, Qingcheng, and Yida Five Money Shops 3. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce

Ministry of Education Explains the Disposal of Assets After the Closure of Private Schools

Handled in Accordance with Article 16 of the Regulations for Private Schools

The Ministry of Education previously received a telegram from Guan Jingcheng, Director of the Education Bureau of Nantong County, requesting an explanation of the handling of school assets and public property in cases where educational administrative organs take over closed private schools. The Ministry of Education responded yesterday by telegram, ordering the director to handle the matter in accordance with Article 16 of the Regulations for Private Schools. (Article 16 of the original text states that if a school established by the board of directors is dissolved and its assets have no owner, the assets shall be disposed of by the competent educational administrative organ.)
