The following is an excerpt from the Implementation Plan for Short-Term Compulsory Education: (1) The Establishment of Provincial and County Experimental Zones and the Division of County and City School Districts: In the first phase of the Implementation Plan for Compulsory Education in Hubei Province, experimental zones for compulsory education were set up in Wuchang, Moyang, Yichang, Shashi, Xiangyang, and Wuxue, with separate zones for urban and rural areas. In addition to the above-mentioned experimental zones, experimental zones for short-term compulsory education will also be set up in Yangyang, Zhongxiang, Shinan, and Anlu for universal experimentation and demonstration. The division of school districts in counties and cities will be based on the standard of autonomous regions. During implementation, it will be carried out in accordance with Article 2 of the Outline of Implementation of Short-Term Compulsory Education, which stipulates that the implementation of short-term compulsory education shall be based on townships, towns, and neighborhoods. If autonomous regions have not yet been delineated, local areas may consider the local population and the distance between children's schools to divide them into several school districts, stipulating that a short-term primary school shall be set up in areas with more than 500 households. (2) The Method of Establishing Short-Term Elementary Schools or Short-Term Elementary Schools: Each provincial experimental zone shall set up 5 to 20 short-term elementary schools, and each public and private complete elementary school above the level of the school shall add at least one short-term elementary school class. Each county experimental zone shall set up 2 to 5 short-term elementary schools, and each county and city school district shall set up several short-term elementary schools, with the number of schools based on the ability to accommodate out-of-school children aged 10 to 16. Encourage various agencies, groups, and individuals to set up short-term elementary schools or short-term elementary school classes. (3) Steps to Promote Short-Term Compulsory Education: Starting from August of this year, it will be carried out in three phases, each phase lasting one year. In the first phase, from August 1932 to July of next year, each provincial experimental zone shall set up several short-term elementary schools, each county shall establish at least two experimental zones, and each experimental zone shall set up two short-term elementary schools. Each public and private complete elementary school above the level of the school shall add one short-term elementary school class. In the second phase, from August of next year to July of the year after next, all short-term elementary schools that should be set up in each provincial experimental zone shall be fully established. In addition to adding two experimental zones in each county, each experimental zone shall set up 2 to 5 short-term elementary schools, and short-term elementary schools shall be set up in each district. During this period, more than one-half of the townships, towns, and neighborhoods under each county shall have one short-term elementary school. Secondly, each county and city shall improve the methods for private schools in each county and convert the improved private schools into substitute elementary schools and add a short-term elementary school class. In the third phase, from August 1934 to July 1935, each county shall complete five experimental zones, and each county and city township, town, and neighborhood shall, in addition to establishing one short-term elementary school, increase the number of short-term elementary schools or short-term elementary school classes if there are still older out-of-school children. Each county and city shall be handled in accordance with the above procedures. If the area belongs to a bandit area or a disaster area or has special circumstances and cannot be held on schedule, the county magistrate may submit an application for approval to extend the period. (Omitted below)

Meeting of Supervisors of the Municipal Education Association

The Municipal Education Association held its first meeting of supervisors at the association's office at 4:00 PM yesterday. The supervisors present were Cheng Kuanzheng, Wu Ren, Qi Zhang Xiaotian, Du Tan, Zheng Tan, and Chen Bai. The alternate supervisors present were Zhang Yousan and Gu Yinqian. Chen Bai presided over the meeting. The meeting proceeded as scheduled. The items discussed were: (1) How to handle the case of Wu Kaixian's letter requesting resignation from the post of executive supervisor concurrently held by him. It was unanimously decided to retain him. (2) Drafting the detailed rules of the association and requesting approval. It was decided to revise and pass them. (3) The staff of the board of directors and supervisors of the association should be generally referred to as clerks to avoid confusion with the secretaries of the education associations in various districts. It was decided to handle this in conjunction with the board of directors. (4) The association's constitution has some incomplete provisions that should be revised. It was decided that the executive supervisors should draft a proposal in conjunction with the executive directors.

The Private School Federation of the French Concession is Actively Carrying Out a Subsidy Movement

Yesterday, the Association Submitted a Petition to the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Education to Argue Their Case Based on Reason

Sudden Prohibition of Broadcasting and Speeches by the British Authorities

The Private School Federation of the French Concession in Shanghai is seeking subsidies from the French Municipal Council for private schools in the concession. Since the Municipal Education Bureau and the Municipal Government negotiated with the French Consul, the federation has been waiting for a solution. However, all parties are still working hard. The recent work is divided as follows:

Document Submitted to the Municipal Government

The federation prepared a document and submitted it to the Municipal Government yesterday to argue their case based on reason. The following is an excerpt from the original text: "We believe that the French Municipal Council should allocate 20% of its total annual income to Chinese education starting in 1933, giving priority to subsidizing private primary and secondary schools that have already been established in the concession, so that they can be expanded to accommodate out-of-school Chinese children. In the past month, we have been appealing in all directions in order to realize our demands and fight for the benefits we deserve. (Omitted) Our federation's movement to request funding from the French Municipal Council was a last resort when we went to petition. Since the Municipal Education Bureau and Your Government have undertaken to negotiate with the French Municipal Council, we can wait quietly for a solution. However, we would like to ask Your Government to strive for the following: The French Municipal Council should seek balanced development for Western and Chinese education in the concession. However, according to the findings of the investigation, the annual education expenses for each Westerner are 44 taels, while the education expenses for each Chinese child are only 7 qian and 22 fen. This is so unfair that it is shocking. Therefore, we request that the French Municipal Council develop Chinese education to make the treatment of Chinese children and Western children equal as a principle. In addition to distributing it to the Municipal Education Bureau, we submit it together for your examination and approval. We respectfully ask Your Government to fight for it based on reason as soon as possible in order to realize it. We await your orders with the utmost urgency."

Broadcasting Not Completed

In order to awaken the public's attention, the federation originally planned to broadcast speeches in Mandarin, English, and French by the executive committee members at the Zhongxi Pharmacy on Sima Road from 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM every Monday and Thursday, starting on the 5th of this month. The arrangements had already been made, and it was about to begin. Unexpectedly, the British Concession Police Department sent detectives to the Zhongxi Pharmacy the day before yesterday to inform them that speeches were prohibited. The federation was outraged when they heard this, because this action was purely to promote the educational cause in the concession, and it did not disrupt the security of the concession or violate the anti-concession prohibition. To be prohibited is extremely unreasonable. In addition to submitting a serious protest to the British Concession authorities through the Municipal Government, the federation will convene a general meeting to discuss effective measures to negotiate with the British Concession authorities.

The Guangzhao Celebrates 20th Anniversary Tomorrow

The Guangzhao Primary and Secondary School on North Sichuan Road has reached its 20th anniversary since its establishment. A commemorative meeting has been specially scheduled for the 4th of this month (the anniversary) at the Rongguang Grand Theater on Haining Road to entertain students, parents, and alumni (but because many of the school addresses have changed, they have been notified in the newspapers). Mayor Wu and others will be invited to give speeches, and there will be excellent films and other entertainment to add to the fun. A dinner party will be held at the Taotao Restaurant in the evening. However, due to the current national crisis, everything will be kept simple, so the various sectors of the city have not been invited to participate.

Thirtieth-First Anniversary of the Patriotic Girls' School

The Patriotic Girls' School has been established for thirty-one years. During the January 28th Incident, when the Japanese invaded Shanghai, the school was located in the war zone, and most of its buildings were destroyed. This semester, amidst the tense atmosphere, the school resolutely moved back, added new buildings, and renovated the gardens, presenting a new look. Yesterday was the school's thirty-first anniversary, and a commemorative ceremony was held in the morning. Attendees included Mao Xiaxuan, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Xu Peihuang, representative of the Mayor, Jin, District Chief of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Cai Zimin and Li Yisheng, school directors, guests Liao Maoru, Wang Zhuanming, and alumni Jin Guangmei, totaling several hundred people. First, Principal Sun Xiangzhong reported on the school's situation and post-recovery plans. Then, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters gave a speech, stating that education must have a revolutionary spirit, and women should pay more attention to education. Afterwards, the Mayor's representative gave a speech, encouraging the school authorities, faculty, and students to embrace the spirit of striving for recovery, so that the imperialists' conspiracy to destroy our cultural institutions would not succeed. Following this, Cai Zimin, the chairman of the board of directors, reported on the difficulties and hardships of the school's initial establishment and the school's contribution to the revolution, hoping to continue this spirit in the future. Afterwards, guest Liao Maoru gave a speech, stating that the educational circles should have: (1) a spirit of moving forward, (2) a spirit of hard work, and (3) a spirit of cooperation, in order to save the declining trend in education and save the country and the nation. Representatives of faculty and students also gave speeches. Afterwards, a group photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned. In the afternoon, a parents' meeting was held, and recreational performances were staged, attracting a large crowd of guests.

Seventeenth International Race Walking of 17 Miles and 100 Yards Held Tomorrow Morning

Starting at 8:00 AM at the Intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Cadre Road

Sixty-One Athletes from Six Countries Participating in Team and Individual Competitions

The British Team's Average Talent Makes Them China's Biggest Enemy

China Must Work Hard to Retain the Championship

The annual Shanghai International Race Walking competition will be held tomorrow morning at 8:00 AM at the old site, the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Cadre Road. The entire route will be the same as before, ending in front of the grandstand of the Racecourse, a total of seventeen miles and one hundred yards. A total of sixty-one athletes from six countries are participating this time, plus individual competitors. The number of British athletes is nearly half of the total, making them unmatched by any other country. The competition will be very intense. The details are listed below.

It Will be Difficult for the Chinese Team to Retain the Championship

The International Race Walking Championship has been held by the Chinese team for three years. This time, due to the loss of two veteran players, although there are new athletes to replace them, the average talent of the British team is strong, and it will be difficult for China to maintain its glory. It is predictable that Shi Jinsheng can win first place and will definitely set a new record. Zhou Yuyu will have difficulty repeating his old form. This year, the British team is China's biggest enemy and intends to regain the championship held by China. It is hoped that the Chinese athletes will work hard for it.

Pacers' Notice

The International Race Walking will be held tomorrow morning, rain or shine. However, in view of the fact that the pacers in the previous session crowded the route and hindered progress, the pacer rules have been slightly changed. Each athlete may have two pacers, but they must pace in sections. The entire course is divided into two sections. The first person is only allowed to join at the intersection of Jisi Feier Road and Bailinan Road (i.e., the Pentagon). They must exit at the intersection of Bielgen Road and Hongqiao Road (i.e., the eight-mile mark) and be replaced by the second person for the second section. The second person must exit at the intersection of Tongfu Road and Weihaiwei Road and go around directly into the Racecourse. The number cloth of the pacer must be on the right arm. All those who serve as pacers should pay attention, and those who serve in the second section can go directly to the intersection of Luo Biejin Road, Hongqiao Road after the departure to wait.

Chinese Referees

In addition to Cheng Yize, Honorary Chairman of the Chinese Team, the Chinese who have been hired by the conference to serve as officials this time also include Yan Siliang, Zhang Guodong, Zhou Jiaqi, Shu Hong, Jiang Xiangqing, Cao Jinzhang, Zhang Zao Cun, Qu Gu Yu, Yu Zhichen, Zhang Zizhen, Shi Youhui, Lu Yutian and others, more than ten people, serving as referees and other duties.

Joint Meeting of the Chinese Team

In addition, the China Race Walking Association, in order to maintain the championship, has decided to hold a joint meeting of athletes and pacers at 2:00 PM today at the Association's location in the Moore Memorial Church on Xizang Road to discuss all the proceedings during the competition. A referee meeting will also be held at the same time to distribute badges, armbands, and allocate vehicles. All Chinese team athletes, pacers, and referees must be on time.

John has been the champion for many years, but this year, the veterans have declined, and the new players have not reached the ideal state, and their strength has decreased. In the other Division A match, Pirates defeated Ye Shi 63 to 24. In the Division B match, John Middle School defeated Tongwen 61 to 8. Six matches tonight.

John Middle School Defeats Tongwen John Middle School's victory over Tongwen College was like striking an egg with a stone. In the first half, Tongwen only scored two points, 33 to 2. In the second half, it was still like entering a no-man's land. The final result was 61 to 8.

Jinan Fights Hard to Break John In the first half, Jinan threw in two goals and made one free throw, with a score of 5 to 0, a powerful momentum. Then they took the lead with 7 to 1. Seeing that the situation was not good, John changed tactics and fought again. Although they gradually saw success, they still trailed by four points at 15 to 11. Hou Xuemin was transferred in and tied the score at 15 to 15. After Chen Xianglong scored one goal, John won the first half with 19 to 15, leading by four points. Starting in the second half, Jinan's attack was particularly fierce. Many fouls were committed, losing a lot of points, only leading by five or six points. When the score was 28 to 23, Chen Xianglong committed four fouls, and John's front line became even more of a mess. Jinan was unstoppable, winning the second half with 38 to 25. John only scored six points in total. Jinan's performance in the second half was compact and very watchable.

Hangzhou Basketball Game Causes a Great Disturbance

Huilan Sports Instructor Leads Students to Assault and Humiliate Referees

Referee Meeting Decides on Severe Punishment, Education Department to Implement Separately

In the Zhejiang First District Games, the high school basketball game between Provincial High School and Private Huilan Middle School was held at the former National Games basketball court. Because it was related to winning the championship, the conference was extremely cautious, and there were as many as five timekeepers. At 9:00 AM, the referee Xu Yingchao blew the whistle to start the game.

Huilan Loses The strength of the two armies was stronger in high school, leading from beginning to end. However, Huilan was not willing to be outdone, so the competition was often tense. The referees enforced the law impartially and meticulously. As a result, Huilan was declared defeated by one point.

Unfortunate Incident After the game, the audience dispersed. Suddenly, Huilan sports instructor Xu Mumin led the students to surround the referee, claiming that the game time was not over. They then rioted and used force, and the referee was unjustly attacked. Fortunately, the staff of the conference went to stop them and were also frequently beaten.

Announcing a Ceasefire After the unfortunate incident occurred, the conference felt that the situation was serious, and it would be difficult for future games to proceed smoothly, so it issued an emergency order to announce a temporary suspension.

Referee Meeting All the referees heard the news and felt that it was extremely unfair for the referee to be humiliated on duty. Therefore, at 7:00 PM that night, an emergency meeting of all the referees was convened. The following resolutions were unanimously passed and sent to the Standing Committee of the First District Games and the Provincial Department of Education for implementation.

(1) Request the Regional Conference and the Provincial Department of Education to cancel Huilan Middle School's participation in all sports meets and competitions and all its representative rights for more than three years. The points and championship won by the school in this district games will also be cancelled. (2) Ask the conference and Huilan Middle School to send a letter of apology to Mr. Xu Yingchao and publish it in the newspaper. (3) Ask the conference and the Education Department to order all schools in the province not to hire Xu Mumin as a sports or other teacher, and send letters to schools and educational institutions across the country not to hire Xu Mumin as any teacher or staff member. (4) Request the Education Department to order Huilan Middle School to immediately terminate Xu Mumin's employment contract. (5) Request the Education Department to order Huilan Middle School to immediately expel the students who took the lead in the attack. (6) The conference and the Education Department will provide a satisfactory reply and implement it conscientiously. Otherwise, no referee will take responsibility. (7) Ask the conference and the Education Department to properly formulate measures to ensure the safety of referees, otherwise all referees will not take responsibility for any sports meets in the future.

Conference Handling After the unexpected incident occurred, Chief Referee Chen Boqing immediately convened an emergency meeting of the Standing Committee to discuss it overnight. In addition to fully accepting the resolutions of the referees, he has worked with the Education Department to implement them separately and effectively.

Qingdao City Builds North China Sports Field

| Expenditure of 100,000 Yuan |

| Expected Completion in April or May |

Qingdao Correspondence: When the 16th North China Games were held in Bian this year, the North China Sports Federation also took the opportunity to hold an annual meeting. The Qingdao representatives, acting on the intention of Mayor Shen, welcomed the 17th North China Games to be held in Qingdao next year. Unexpectedly, the representatives from Shanxi Province also had the same request at that time. After deliberation by the Executive Committee, it was decided that Shanxi Province had requested it first last year, so the next North China Games should be given priority to be held in that province, but it was necessary to build a large-scale stadium as a prerequisite. The Municipal Government received a letter from the North China Sports Federation yesterday, stating that according to a letter from the Shanxi Provincial Government, the province had suffered a severe flood and was currently engaged in various relief efforts, making it difficult to prepare. They requested that it be held in Qingdao. It is reported that the Municipal Government decided to reply with a letter of welcome. Regarding the construction of the stadium, planning is currently underway. A preparatory committee will be established to be responsible for preparing everything, and the Municipal Government has decided to allocate 100,000 yuan as construction costs. The construction site has been surveyed in the eastern part of the Huiquan Racecourse and part of the First Park to create a large-scale public stadium, which is expected to be completed in April or May next year.

Middle School Cross-Country Race

Held at Jinan University on the 21st of this Month

The Cross-Country Running Committee of the Shanghai Secondary School Sports Federation held a meeting at the YMCA yesterday. The attendees were Hao Chunde (Chairman), Leng Yang (Record), and Chen Guangzi. After discussion, it was decided that the location had been decided by the conference to be held at Jinan University. The resolutions are listed on the left: (1) The date is set for December 21st at 3:00 PM. (2) The stipulated distance is 5,000 meters. (3) The number of participants per school shall be no more than ten and no less than six. (4) Scoring method: A. The team score is calculated by six people. B. The ranking is calculated as the score (the lower the better). The team with the lowest score wins. (5) The conference staff will be hired by Committee Member Hao Chunde. (6) Registration is from today until 6:00 PM on the 16th. (7) The registration location is at Hao Chunde's office at Jinan University.

Fluctuations in Finance and the Gold Market

| Moving in Accordance with International News |

(A Difference of Fourteen Taels: Yesterday's Gold Market Saw Major Changes and Chaos, Unstoppable Momentum. Although the Daily Difference Was Not as Large as the Previous Day, It Still Reached Fourteen Taels. New High Prices Were Repeatedly Seen, and Finally, There Was a Slight Drop of One Tael and Four Mace. The Will of the Industry Was Extremely Wavering, So the Demand and Supply Were Still Complicated, Largely Moving with the Wind. The Issue of War Debts Was Still Brewing, So the News Varied. From the Early Morning, There Was a Decline Because Exchange Rates Frequently Rose by More Than Three Fen. Although the Silver Market Fell, It Did Not Stimulate a Good Response. Afterwards, There Were Frequently Twists and Turns of Three or Four Taels. In the Middle, the Sudden News That U.S. Bonds Could Be Used to Offset the Currencies of Various Countries for Repayment, and the Sudden Strengthening of the Typhoon, Led to a Downturn. It Once Broke Through the 800 Taels Mark. However, the Trend of Foreign Exchange Rates Was Tense, Especially British Gold. At Noon Closing, News Was Suddenly Heard That War Debts Must Be Demanded, and the Market Sentiment Suddenly Reached Its Peak, Jumping Up Ten Taels in an Instant. The After-Market Reached 813 Taels and Five Mace, Opening a New Record for This Year. Afterwards, Many Parties Took the Opportunity to Sell Off. Furthermore, as Exchange Bills Seemed to Turn Flat, They Instantly Fell by Eight or Nine Taels. Afterwards, It Regained Strength, Standing Between 806 and 807 Taels. Swap Transactions in the Morning: Hengxing Swapped in 70 Units from Tongfengheng, Posting Nine Mace; Huiyuan Swapped in 35 Units, Posting Eight and a Half Mace; It Was Also Heard That Qianchangxiang Swapped in More Than 100 Units, Posting One Tael. The Following Is a Record of the Entire Day's Situation.

The Opening Plunged Four Taels: The Opening Price for January Delivery Was 803 Taels and Three Mace, Down Four Taels and Four Mace. Then, It Increased from Two Taels and Eight Mace to Four Taels and Three Mace. It Was Then Learned That Forward Silver Prices and Private Telegrams Had Both Fallen. Huge Amount of Silver Dollars Loaded on Dalian

| Three Million and Five Thousand |

There Has Been No News of Silver Dollars Loaded on Dalian for a Week. Securities and Bond Market Suddenly Reversed Yesterday

Each Fell by About Two and a Half Yuan

Transaction Volume Was 13 Million

Yesterday (2nd), the Spot Market for Various Bonds on the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange Was Very Desolate. Only the Compilation and Dispatch of the 19th Customs, Finance, and 20th Customs Were Slightly Opened. The Remaining Had No Market. Futures Trading Was Still Active. The Market Price Fell Sharply, and Buying and Selling Inflow and Outflow Were Active. Checking the Market Price of Each Bond, Since the Last Few Weeks, They Have Risen One After Another by About 10 Yuan. The Strength of the Rising Momentum Is Only Seen Within the Year. Until Yesterday, the Reversal Began. The Market Had Large Households Selling and Profit-Taking, and The Market Situation Suddenly Changed. Once the Selling Interest Was Strong, Each Price Fell Very Sharply. Each Plate Fell Step by Step, and the Trend Was Exhausted. Carefully Observing the Current Market Conditions of Bonds, They Are Generally Quite Good, So If There Are No Other Major Reasons Affecting the Market, There Will Not Be a Greater Drop. New York Stock Market Recovers

Shanghai Xinfeng Foreign Firm Report, Thursday (1st), the New York Stock Market Trended Upward Again. Wheat Was Reported Up More Than 2 Fen, and the British Pound Continued to Recover. People's Hearts All Felt Good. However, Because the Parliament Will Be Meeting Next Week, and How the War Debt Issue Will End, It Is Difficult to Predict. So, Generally, Everyone Adopted a Wait-and-See Attitude, Which Led to Weak Transactions. The Total Number of Transactions for the Entire Day Was 800,000. Also, the Broker's Loan Released This Week Was 358 Million Yuan, Which Was 8 Million Yuan More Than Last Week. The Interest Rate on 60-Day and 90-Day Loans Was 0.075. The Dow Jones Index Is Listed on the Left.

Closing Price Compared to the Previous Day

Thirty Industrial Stocks 58.02 Rose 1.67

Twenty Railroad Stocks 25.75 Rose 1.71

Twenty Utility Stocks 26.60 Rose 0.25

Forty Bonds 77.25 Rose 0.04

Yarn and Cloth Market Hardens

Gold Price Rises Sharply, People's Hearts Are Optimistic

The Base Has Already Small, and Long Sentiment Is Strong

Cotton Yarn Market Situation: Firm, Because the Sharp Rise in Gold Prices Has Made People's Hearts Good. Scattered Shorts Take the Opportunity to Cover, and the Market Sentiment Is Becoming More and More Tense. There Is Also a Part of the Base That Has Already Become Small, and There Is a Slight Long Sentiment, But the Actual Demand Is Still Stagnant, Which Is Inevitably a Flaw.

The Human Standard Is Good Eight or Nine Qian: At the Opening of the Previous Market for the Human Standard, the Market Sentiment Was Still Flat. In the Second and Third Rounds, It Was Heard That the Gold Market Was Trending Upward, and Each Month Rose by 2, 4, 6, and 8 Qian. The Afternoon Situation Was Still Good, and Each Month Rose by Another 1, 2, 3, and 4 Qian. The Total Transaction Volume for the Entire Day Was 20,500 Bales. Checking the Sales, Hengchang Sold 700 Bales, Dachang 350 Bales, Yongda 300 Bales, Shenji 400 Bales, and Tongyu 350 Bales. The Buyers Were Yukang 700 Bales, Dafeng 500 Bales, Mingde 700 Bales, Shenji 600 Bales, Yuantai 650 Bales, Changfeng 800 Bales, and Yiyu 1,100 Bales. The Closing Prices Are Listed Below.

Cotton Market Trend Is Increasingly Tight

Gold Price Rises, U.S. Exchange Rate Shrinks, U.S. Cotton Secretly Raises

| Long Activities, Scattered Shorts Supplement |

The Cotton Market Is Trending Upward, and the Situation Is Becoming Increasingly Tight. Because the Gold Market Rises Sharply and the U.S. Exchange Rate Shrinks Wildly, U.S. Cotton Secretly Raises. Therefore, Those Who Do Long Are Also Active. A Part of the Scattered Shorts Supplements. However, The Attitude of a Certain Manufacturer Is Still Calm, Without Any Intention of Supplementing Shorts. The Future of the Cotton Market Is Lacking in Grasp.

Recent Cotton Rises by Two Qian and a Half: At the Opening of the Previous Market for Zheng Standard, the Market Sentiment Was Tight. Each Month Rose by 5 Fen to 1 Qian. In the Afternoon, It Was Heard That Gold Prices Were High Again, and the Situation Was Still Good. Each Month Rose by 1 Qian. The Transaction Volume for the Entire Day Was Estimated to Be 38,200 Dan. Checking the Sales, Changji Sold 5,600 Dan, and Xincheng 1,100 Dan. The Buyers Were Mingde 2,300 Dan, Changhe 1,200 Dan, Suilong 1,200 Dan, Yiyu 1,700 Dan, and Yifeng 1,300 Dan, 1,200 Dan, Yiyu 1,700 Dan, and Yifeng 1,300 Dan, Dachang 1,000 Dan. U.S. Cotton Southern Continue Have Hedge Selling

Yesterday, U.S. Cotton Was Weak at First Due to Southern Hedge Selling, and Then Recovered Due to Fellow Traders Buying and Short Covering. The Estimated Futures Increase and Decrease Was One to Two Pounds. Spot Goods Did Not Move. British Cotton Futures Fell One Point, and Spot Goods Fell Eleven Points. Egyptian Cotton Spot Goods Fell Fifteen Points. Indian Cotton Japanese Merchants Bought In, and the Market Situation Was Stable. It Is Estimated That Pingguoer and Bailuoxi Fell 2.25 Robbies. U.S. Cotton Private Estimates Increased Again

1st, New York Telegram. Fanqueer Announced the New Cotton Estimate for This Season, the Production Amount Is 12,227,000 Bales, Which Is 611,000 Bales More Than the Last Time (November 1st). Also, The Number of Ginned Cotton Is 11,075,000 Bales.

Food, River Down, Rice Market South Fixed North Exhausted

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, More Than 40 Sources Came from the Xiang Road Groups. The Store Parties Took This Opportunity to Put Guns to Heads, Added to the Inventory, and People's Hearts Turned Around. Thin Rice Slightly Had Storage Households Coming to Stacks and Hardening by Several Fen. The Sales of Su and Tong Groups Were Flat and the Price Was Set. The Change in Yin Yuan Led to Prosperous Sales and Light Sales, and the Situation Presented a Downstream Phenomenon.

(New Zha) Yesterday, More Than 50 Inland Arrivals on the Suzhou River. The Store Stomachs in This Street Were Relaxed. Goods From Changshu and Kunshan Fell by 2 Jiao at the Opening. Early Rice Also Followed Lowering by Nearly a Foot. Dudu Pointed Customer Groups Slightly Moved, And Also Tightly Escorted Permits. The Daily Corn Foot Was About 2,500 Dan.

Starch Fiercely Raises

| The Tianjin Group Slightly Flattens After Returning Before Closing |

After the Opening of the Starch Market Yesterday Morning, Each Month Showed a Fiercely Rising State. With the Foreign Wheat Quote, The U.S. Soared by 7 or 8 Jiao, and the Ridge Rose by 2 or 3 Jiao. Coupled with the Remaining Wind of the High Gold Market, The Hearts of Most People Were Consistently Firm. The Near and Far Opening Prices Were Invisibly Raised by 2 or 3 Fen Compared to the Previous Day's Closing. Transactions in Each Plate Were Smooth and Prosperous. The Long-Term Was Particularly Spectacular Because People's Hearts Had Already Turned to Rise. Until the Beginning of the Afternoon Opening, It Was Also Good, Then It Was Slightly Soft in the Midst of Consolidation. Because of the Return of the Tianjin Group, A Small Number of Small and Medium-Sized Factories Also Had a Small Number of Shipments (It Is Said That Tianjin Continued to Order More Than 200,000 Bags of Australian Flour at a Price of 1 Tael, 6 Qian, and 6 or 7 Fen). So, People's Hearts Were Slightly Flat. However, Dalian Did a Lot, and It Was Also Related to the Rescue. Observing the Subsequent Steps, After This Rise, It Should Temporarily Trend Towards Stabilization. The Result Was This Month Rose by 1 Fen and 7 Li and a Half Compared to the Previous Day. January Rose by 2 Fen and 2 Li and a Half. February Rose by 3 Fen and a Half. March Rose by 3 Fen. April Rose by 3 Fen and 2 Li and a Half. May Opened at 1 Tael, 7 Qian, and 7 Fen, and the Closing Price Was Also Good by 1 Fen.

Futures Wheat Has Smooth Transactions and Prices Soar

Yesterday's Futures Wheat Market, Each Month Unanimously Presented a Soaring Phenomenon. With the Foreign Wheat Quote, It Recovered and Rose by 2 or 3 Jiao to 7 or 8 Jiao. The Exchange Rate Stepped Downward. This Situation Inevitably Impedes the Future of Fixed Wheat. The Exchange, Which Had Been Silent for a Long Time, Finally Showed a Glimmer of Life. The Transactions in Each Plate in the Morning and Afternoon Were Smooth and Prosperous, and Market Prices Also Soared Wildly. Observing the Future, If There Is No Foreign Wheat Hedging, It Is Difficult to Loosen. The Result Was This Month Rose by 7 Fen Compared to the Previous Day. January Rose by 4 Fen. February Rose by 7 Fen. March Rose by 6 Fen. April Rose by 7 Fen.

Sugar Market Sugar Goods Rise with the Gold Price

Yesterday, Because the Standard Gold Suddenly Rose to 813 Taels, The Sugar Market Was Tense, and Each Sugar Unanimously Rose High. The Association Drew the Plate, and the Ordinary Goods of No. 24 Coarse Silicon White Were Drawn at 15 Taels and 6 Qian, Which Was 2 Qian Higher Than the Previous Day. High Goods 15 Taels and 7 Qian. No. 18 Medium Sand White 14 Taels and a Half, Which Was 2 Qian Higher Than the Previous Day. No. 20 Medium

North-South Goods: Almond Prices Improve, Shanghai Market Stagnant

Almond sales have been quite sluggish recently, with little price fluctuation. According to letters from Tianjin, prices have gradually increased. White Jade Flat almonds are priced at 52 taels, Dragon King Hat at 46 taels, Wilderness Almonds are out of stock at the origin, North Mountain Almonds at 37 taels, and Nine-Ridge Eyebrow at 35 taels. Adding all external fees, the prices are similar to those in Shanghai. However, the trading volume here is minimal, and merchants are not interested in further procurement. Yesterday's market prices were: White Jade Flat 60 taels, King Hat 53-54 taels, Wilderness Almonds 48-49 taels, North Mountain Almonds 45 taels, and Nine-Ridge Eyebrow 41-42 taels. The overall trend is flat and weak.

Free Talk

Short Story

Wedding Night (2)

— Bing Xin

She didn't know how many times she had said such words. At first, she felt a bit sentimental and sometimes even shed tears, but later she didn't even have a sad expression. She was already thirty-six years old, but her sallow face made her look like an old woman who was at least forty-five or forty-six. She had no family and was just doing odd jobs for people, mending clothes, combing hair to make a living. She didn't owe debts and had never lived a comfortable life. Because she was an unfortunate person, she was always forbidden to watch whenever someone had a wedding, and she was very self-aware, never going to see the bride until the next day.

(Sister Lian, congratulations on getting a good sister-in-law. I heard she's very beautiful, like a fairy descended from heaven.)

Sister-in-law Xun quickly bowed to Sister Lian to congratulate her, but Sister Lian replied with disappointment:

(She is very beautiful, but she is too young and doesn't understand anything. She even made a joke last night. Did you hear it?)

(I heard it. But it doesn't matter. Last night was the first night, and traditionally the new bride is supposed to be polite. It will be better tonight. As long as the two of them are familiar with each other, there will be no problems.)

Sister-in-law Xun spoke as if she had a lot of experience.

(Yes! You're still worrying about them. Maybe they are at this moment...)

The Old Lady Ru's two sentences were so powerful that they not only made them laugh until their stomachs hurt, but even the guests next door and the next door neighbor were awakened by the laughter! (2)

The bride, Miss Xiu, was just as everyone praised, like a fairy descended from heaven. She had all the beautiful qualities of a woman, but one thing that must be said was a shortcoming: she never dared to look people in the eye when she spoke, but just stared at the ground, and sometimes she stuttered and stammered. In short, watching her speak was uncomfortable, but perhaps some people would appreciate another kind of charm from this, so it is said that several handsome young men had suffered lovesickness for her.

Miss Xiu's father was a Daoist with incense offerings. He was very honest and intelligent, and had believed in the Buddha since he was a child, so chanting for the Buddha and performing rituals became his lifelong occupation. He had two daughters and three sons. Miss Xiu was the eldest and helped her mother with housework since she was little. The clothes and diapers of her younger siblings were almost entirely taken care of by her. Her temper was very good, and she always smiled at people and never cursed at people. However, she had a strange and unusual belief: that was not to marry!

This is how it happened: when she was fifteen years old, she suddenly started menstruating in the summer. Her mother was very happy because this was a sign of complete development, and she no longer worried that she was infertile (Note 2). However, Miss Xiu was so troubled by this that she almost wanted to commit suicide, because she felt that this thing was not only dirty but also too troublesome. The weather was hot, and she could only wear one pair of pants. If she was not careful, bright red blood would run out regardless of everything, and people would laugh their heads off if they saw it. What if Miss Xiu's mother found out? That would be even worse! Therefore, she felt that menstruation was more terrible than floods and wild beasts. She didn't know that this was a woman's physiological change. When menstruation came, she would feel dizzy, have blurred vision, have weak limbs, and those with problems would have stomachaches, backaches, poor appetite, irritable temper, and all kinds of morbidities would come out together. She only felt inexplicably annoyed, and sometimes even said to herself: (I wish I could die sooner, women are really not human beings!)

Crying

Yesterday came a (laugh), today, let's try another (cry). Although (cry) is somewhat unlucky, and seems to contradict the (total mobilization of laughter) advocated yesterday. But in such a poignant and yet inspiring era, if we are allowed to laugh, then no one can forbid us to cry, as long as we ourselves are not afraid of bad luck.

Speaking of crying, just like laughing, it can be divided into many kinds: The wife of Hua Zhou Qi Liang was good at crying for her husband, which was the sorrowful cry of a widow; Jia Baoyu accidentally said a word or two that offended his sister, and Lin Daiyu would cover her face and hum and sob, which was a flirtatious cry; When Zeng Zi died, Zeng Xi actually lost his sight because of crying for his son, which was a genuine cry originating from nature; When King Xiang of Chu bid farewell to Yu Ji at Wujiang and sang loudly (Yu Xi, Yu Xi, what can I do?) and his voice and tears fell together, that was the tragic cry of a hero at the end of his road; As for the amorous Emperor Chen Houzhu who complained to people and said (I wash my face with tears here every day), that was a depressed cry recalling past glory; As for A Dou, the crown prince, who finished reciting in front of Emperor Wu of Jin, (The tombs of my ancestors are far away in Min and Shu...) Because he had no tears, he closed his eyes tightly to replace the cry, which was the child's fake cry, which was despicable and unworthy of mention.

However, let us not underestimate crying! The use of crying is very great! So great that it has unexpected effects! Look at Shen Baoxu of the State of Chu, who moved the (righteous indignation) of the State of Qin by crying for three days - but perhaps it was out of compassion, and the righteous army was dispatched, and the State of Chu, which had already perished, was able to be restored as a result. This kind of crying is extraordinary! Ah, just think, crying for three days, how difficult that is! This kind of crying, not to mention the State of Qin, even heaven and earth should be moved by it, and if ghosts and gods are conscious, they should cry with him, which is in accordance with the laws of heaven and human nature! However, Shen Baoxu is already an (ancient person) after all, and the present world seems to be a bit different from the (Era of the Seven Kingdoms). Therefore, when the Japanese soldiers silently seized half of our Northeast territory last year, although a certain gentleman had (grief and indignation) because of it, and a certain commander had (sobbing and speechless) because of it, they could not cry for three days after all; Because they could not cry for three days, although the cries of the two gentlemen originated from the heart, and condensed into tears, and their loyalty and sincerity were such that Heaven could testify, the League of Nations seemed to be too far inferior to the State of Qin after all, and was always unwilling to show compassion and pry open Japan's greedy mouth, to reclaim our Northeastern territory that was complete and intact!

From New York to London

— Wu

If someone came to London from New York and compared the lives of these two cities, I think he would feel a great difference.

The first is the slowness of life, such as the delivery of telephones, letters, transportation, the waiters in the hotel, and the shop assistants in the store, their movements are unhurried. Compared to the Americans who cut the Gordian knot quickly, we can say that London is all in a state of sleep. The second is that London has all kinds of classes: in hotels, restaurants, shops, and on the roads, we can find countless classes. As for the government, it goes without saying. This is their history, tradition, and habits, completely without the appearance of equality on the surface like New York. Nothing is unified or connected, and everything is unnecessarily complicated. The third is the incomplete equipment. In New York, due to the progress of modern scientific civilization, all material enjoyment is rapidly becoming complete; on the contrary, London's life, its scientific civilization, seems to be a century behind, making us feel very lacking in our daily lives. The fourth is the stagnation of the people's character. Compared with the Americans who are quick-witted, straightforward and sharp, they are really lagging behind. For example, when speaking, they are always mumbling and squeaking, unable to distinguish black and white immediately, which can simply drive people crazy. Sixth, there is unbearable melancholy. This will make your whole nerve feel heavy. For example, if you have breathed in the clear air of New York and suddenly come to London's humid and overcast weather, can you not feel excessively melancholy? If you feel like you were a lark soaring in the blue sky in New York, then in London you are like a nightingale groping in the dark.

In short, life in New York is diligent and full of struggle, while life in London is long and lazy.

X X X X X

Forgiveness

— Chuang

Relying on the vague image of you reborn in my soul, I feel that I still like you the most.

Although you once ruined the dawn of my youth, I will never forget your eyes until I die, and even more unforgettable is your clear and gentle voice, which unusually penetrated into my heart, and my chest trembled for a long, long time, like a lonely zither being plucked by slender fingers.

Ah! I know many women, they have bright red lips, their foreheads are delicate, and their words are gentle.

My friends will tell you that I sing for them, but my mother will tell you that I cry for you.

I cry, but my tears have gradually become scarce;

I used to wail, but now I only shed tears;

As I get older, my eyes will become stingy, and one day my sorrow will only be a kind of boredom.

Yes, because you once broke the flower of my youth, when I am old, I may hate you.

I hope your image will always be reborn in my soul! I hope that when I remember your eyes, I can deeply forgive you!

(Translated by Sully Prudhomme)

Suspended Flying Railway

— Qiong

We are now in the Speedy era, and all undertakings value speed. In addition to trams, trains, automobiles, and subways, there are even faster airplanes.

Of course, today's airplanes are becoming more and more safe, and they are indeed a hundred times more advanced than before. However, if the machine parts are damaged, there is still a risk of falling, and it is also bound by the weather. For example, wind and rain are unfavorable for flight. Therefore, there is now an invention of a high-speed and very safe suspended flying tram. This is a transportation tool that is not hindered by the weather and travels in the air.

The Suspended Flying Railway, in English, is called RailPlane, and was invented by the British George Bening. Recently, taking advantage of the British Transportation Conference, it was put into trial operation. Because it is a trial operation, of course, the horsepower cannot be too high, but the speed is still 190 kilometers per hour. Undoubtedly, this is an astonishing Speedy.

As for the construction cost, it is also very low. According to Bening's calculation, if it is calculated in units of 1,000 kilometers, it only costs 150,000 to 190,000 yuan (approximately 250,000 to 300,000 yuan per mile), so compared with the underground railway, which costs 4 million yuan per mile, the suburban railway, which costs 500,000 yuan per mile, and the urban tram, which costs 700,000 to 1 million yuan, it is indeed much cheaper.

This flying car not only has the above-mentioned amazing speed, but is also very safe. Originally, the car body was suspended in the air on a track, and there was also a safety net below, so that even if there was a machine failure, it would not fall.

The exterior and interior of the car body are similar to those of an airship. Both the front and rear are equipped with propellers to increase the speed of flight.

What I Have Seen of French Women

— Ice Lady

When French women are mentioned, I think many people must think that they are the most extravagant and licentious women in the world. Before I went to France, I also thought so; but after living in France for a few years, I realized that this was a big mistake.

French women do love to be pretty, but they are definitely not extravagant. After the war, most French women had to support themselves because they had lost their husbands or could not find husbands. Their lives were very difficult. It goes without saying that they would not be extravagant; even women who were well-off and did not have to work outside lived a very frugal life. Most of the housework is handled by the housewife herself, and very few servants are hired. I did not see any servants in the homes of several professors I visited in Paris and the surrounding areas. The professors' wives got up early every day, carried a bag to the market to buy this and that, and then came back to clean the house, mop the floor, cook, and do laundry... They were busy from morning to night, without a moment's rest. Compared with Chinese women, whose husbands earn forty or fifty yuan a month and hire maids, while they themselves are full all day long and do nothing, it is really unknown where the diligence and thrift have gone!

Furthermore, French women also have a commendable quality: they do not regard work as a shameful thing. When I was in Paris, I lived in the home of a music teacher for a few months through the introduction of a friend. This music teacher was an old maid who was almost forty years old. She lived with her old mother. She taught piano and earned about a thousand francs a month in tuition fees. In addition, she could earn three hundred francs a month in rent. When French people rent out their houses, they don't just give you a bare house like Chinese people, and don't care about anything. They not only have to provide the tenants with all the necessary utensils, but also have to serve the tenants. The music teacher I lived with had no servants, so everything in the house was done by the music teacher herself. Every morning, before her female students who studied piano came, she had to make my bed, dust, mop the floor, pour wash water, and do all kinds of chores. This must be a very strange thing in the eyes of Chinese women, a music teacher pouring wash water and mopping the floor for others! But in the eyes of French women, this is very normal. When the old lady cleaned my room, she jumped around and sometimes sang in a low voice, without feeling that this was a shameful thing at all. After she poured the wash water and mopped the floor, she went to teach other people's piano, without losing her status at all. I think this spirit is what Chinese women should quickly emulate.

Furthermore, most Chinese people think that French women are licentious, which is also a mistake. Foreigners who have only traveled around Paris for a few days see those grotesque women sitting in cafes and say that French women are so and so licentious, which is inevitably close to dogmatism. According to my observation, French women, compared with women from other European countries, are considered to be the most restrained and conservative. Young girls from middle-class and above families are not easy to get close to men, and they are often accompanied by someone when they go out; even the French female students in universities are not as casual as female students from other countries in socializing with male students. In fact, if you compare French women with the so-called modern ladies in China - often modern ladies who dance with their boyfriends until late at night before returning home - the word (licentious) cannot be applied to French women at all.

I am not writing this short article to praise the virtues of French women; I am only doing so because I have returned after living abroad for many years, and I have seen that Chinese women (I am of course using women from the middle class as the standard) have indeed made much more progress in terms of decoration than before, but in reality, not to mention those who have not received education; those who have received education - except for a very few - still only know how to play mahjong, eat big meals, dance, and watch movies? This phenomenon is really heartbreaking, so I couldn't help but write this pile of harsh words.

Submission Guidelines

(1) This journal welcomes the following types of manuscripts, and will pay generously upon publication:

(1) Humorous writing with profound meaning, within 400 words.

(2) Translated short stories of world-renowned works.

(3) Short original fiction with substantial content and artistic value.

(4) Writing discussing issues related to women, families, children, and youth.

(5) Anecdotes of scientists, invention stories, and accessible and interesting science introductions.

(6) Descriptions of customs and cultures from countries around the world.

(7) Travelogues and impression pieces with beautiful writing and unique insights.

(2) Submissions should preferably be written in spoken language, neatly handwritten, and punctuated with the new style. For translations, the original work must be attached; if the original work is inconvenient to attach, the title, author, and publisher must be specified in detail.

(3) The name to be published for submissions is at the author's discretion, but the real name and detailed address must be indicated at the end of the manuscript, and stamped with a seal for verification when receiving payment.

(4) Manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. However, this does not apply to long manuscripts of more than 5,000 words that are accompanied by return postage.

(5) The editor reserves the right to edit and modify submissions.

(6) Once a manuscript is published, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

(7) Any plagiarism or manuscripts that have already been published elsewhere will have their remuneration revoked upon discovery.

Long Original Creations

Crossroads of the Era and Love - Part 3

— Zhang Ziping

What a great opportunity! Professor Zeng has returned to Hong Kong to see his second wife. He won't be back for two weeks. Old Lin, this is truly a good chance!

(You're talking nonsense!)

Haiquan continued to ponder, could it be that Old Tang truly saw through his inner thoughts? He could swear that he held no expectations of Crane Child (Tsuruko) beyond the ordinary. However, recently, the image of Crane Child often appeared in his mind, which was a genuine fact. As for why her beautiful image had invaded his consciousness, he was at a loss. Moreover, her image appeared more and more frequently, and the color of the image became increasingly deeper and richer.

(Lately, haven't I been wanting to go home from school early? The clear purpose is to see her...)

Thinking of this, he felt a little ashamed again.

(...Could this be what is called love?)

He sat in the car thinking for a long time, only to realize that the atmosphere around him was a bit cold. The morning had been filled with warm sunshine. After lunch, the sky was densely covered with deep gray, chaotic clouds. The cold wind of early winter swept up the dust and sand on the road, hitting him from the side. He felt a slight shiver and his face felt rough.

He took his hand out of his pocket and touched his cheeks.

Professor Zeng's residence was at the northern end of F Bridge, right behind the nine-story Western-style apartment building. The car stopped in front of the Zeng residence. Haiquan had just paid the fare and was about to press the doorbell when Crane Child came out from inside and opened the outer iron gate.

(Mr. Lin, are you cold?)

(I didn't expect the weather to change so quickly, Aunt Zeng.)

(Oh dear, you're calling me "aunt" again. I really don't want to be so old).

She said with a smile, then followed him inside. As soon as they stepped into the living room, they felt a wave of warmth; it turned out the furnace in the hall had coal added and was burning.

(It's too late today. I must get a stove installed in your room tomorrow).

She said this after asking him to sit down.

(No need for a stove. I don't want a stove in my room. I'm not afraid of the cold).

(Mr. Lin, I heard your teacher say that Shanghai is much colder than your southern climate. Without a stove, you can't get through the winter). Haiquan also felt that the weather in Shanghai was much colder than in the South. According to the lunar calendar, it was only mid-November, but it felt like December in the south.

(Installing a stove is certainly desirable, but I'm afraid it will cost a lot of money. The money for the stove is limited. But burning coal for a winter is indeed not an easy burden. There are many people in my family, and expenses are high. My father's income is just enough for expenses each year. Fortunately, my brother-in-law provides a little support. Otherwise, how could I have come to Shanghai to attend university?)

He was lost in thought when he suddenly heard Crane Child calling him.

(Mr. Lin, you have several letters. I was so busy talking to you that I forgot about your letters).

As she spoke, she stood up, walked to the desk by the window, opened a drawer, took out three letters, and handed them to Haiquan.

He took them and saw that one was a family letter from his old father, one was from his elder sister, and one was from his brother-in-law's younger sister, Liu Peizhu. The father's letter was the most ordinary, simply saying that if possible during the New Year holiday, he should return to his hometown to see his family, primarily because his old grandmother hoped very much that he would return and celebrate the New Year happily with everyone. However, the sister's letter surprised him a little, because this letter was not sent from Guangzhou as before, but from Hong Kong.

(Has their family moved to Hong Kong)?

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

What's Going On?

— Fo

Since the theft and sale case at the Palace Museum, what is the true story behind the scenes? It's truly baffling, leaving people scratching their heads. Was it theft and sale, or not? If it was, who were the thieves? And did they sell 300,000 items, or 700,000, or even more? Were the items sold truly discarded objects with feudal-era characteristics, or were things that were not discarded and did not have feudal characteristics also stolen and sold? This case has been going on for a long time, and it's still a mystery. Recently, the Control Yuan sent personnel to investigate and prepare for impeachment, but it will probably be difficult to completely clarify the situation. Such a serious case of theft and sale is like a headless murder. We must ask detective expert Sherlock Holmes to investigate.

Before this case is resolved, there is suddenly talk of moving the Palace Museum's antiquities to Luoyang. Stealing and selling antiquities is one matter, and moving antiquities is another. But are these two cases related, or are they completely unrelated? Outsiders naturally find it even more unfathomable and difficult to understand the truth. However, according to recent news reports, the news about moving antiquities is quite bizarre. According to a Beijing dispatch on the 24th, all sectors of Beijing opposed the relocation of antiquities to Luoyang and issued five reasons, which seemed quite reasonable. On the 30th, there were two more Beijing dispatches, one from Yi Peiji denying the relocation of Palace Museum antiquities to Luoyang, and one from Chu Minyi stating that Palace Museum antiquities would be moved to Luoyang. Who is advocating for the relocation after all? And for what reason is it necessary to move them to Luoyang? And who are the people who are advocating against it? Are the five reasons given truly factual? This kind of mystery can only be solved by going to the City God Temple to ask for a divination slip.

In short, "roaming the sea as a pirate" is something the ancients warned against. Now I don't blame anyone else. I only blame our country for having too many antiquities, and the antiquities being too good. Not only do foreigners covet them, but even Chinese people are thinking about turning them around. It's truly like the two common sayings, "telling a beggar to hide, there's no place to put them" and "black eyes see white silver." I am very worried about these things and feel sorry for them.

A Manager with Influence

— Yijing Studio Owner

In an office, a glass window horizontally shields a narrow loft. In a corner of the loft, piles of various-colored account books are stacked high. Next to the loft, Manager Wang, around forty years old, sits in a swivel chair. His clothes are dull and lusterless, and a large piece of the cuff is torn, revealing the cotton inside.

The Western-style door slowly opened, and a thin, sallow-faced young clerk walked in, wearing a tattered free-cloth robe. He spoke with pleading sobs: "Mr. Wang, tomorrow is my father's sixtieth birthday. I was hoping to ask for a few days off to go back to my hometown. Please grant my request."

"Impossible. Impossible," Manager Wang replied with a frown.

"Mr. Wang, this is my father's special occasion. Please allow me this time. I promise I won't go again," the thin young man pleaded tremulously.

"Bah! Stop your rambling! If you want to go, then just quit! Alright, and don't bother coming back. There are plenty of people here; we can manage without you. Hahaha, people as poor as you have no right to celebrate birthdays. You'd be better off saving your money." Manager Wang showed his disgust at the man's nagging.

"Yes! I won't go," the thin young man's head slowly drooped. Tears welled in his eyes as he said this and walked out, crestfallen.

Next, a young clerk in a Western suit walked in, his steps...

"Mr. Zhang, please sit down, please sit down," Manager Wang said with a nodding smile.

"Mr. Wang, I want to go back to my hometown today because the day after tomorrow is my uncle's fiftieth death anniversary," the young man in the Western suit said with an air of importance.

"Excellent, excellent. You should go home when there's a family matter. You and I are close friends, there's no reason to refuse you. You don't need to be so polite." Manager Wang replied hurriedly.

"Goodbye, goodbye," the young man in the Western suit said triumphantly and left.

Literature

Lament of Unemployment

— Qin Nan

This summer, a certain gentleman graduated from high school and often visited my residence. Whenever we discussed his background, he would sigh deeply. This poem is written to record his situation.

I remember when I was young, I entered a private school, and studied the Analects and Mencius in order. My father also knew the importance of modern times and ordered me to study new subjects. After four years of primary school, I happily graduated, smiling and pointing to my diploma, I said to him, "I was illiterate when I was young, only knowing how to till the fields. Now you have studied for seven or eight years, your knowledge is a hundred times higher than mine. From now on, you only need to choose a skill, and you will have no worries for the rest of your life." At that time, I was only thirteen years old, able to look at both sides and express my aspirations. But today's affairs are so chaotic, and young people seek knowledge haphazardly. The new system of junior high school has a short term, and the burden does not require large sums. Parents love their children sincerely, so they let the studies be interrupted halfway. In autumn, they send me to the city. The east and west winds are bleak, and the rain is misty. I struggle to pay for food and lodging, and my son can study diligently with peace of mind. Time flies like an arrow, year after year, my grades are listed at the forefront, and my reputation is brilliant. Hiring letters arrive every day, advising me to teach at the neighboring elementary school. But the salary is meager, and the monthly income of ten gold is not enough. A man should have high ambitions. Having obtained Long, can I not hope for Shu again? High school is expected to be completed, and parents are overjoyed to hear this. My family had no fertile fields, so where could I get the money to provide for me? Alas, the efforts to raise money were now like a dream. I finally looked forward to graduation, and my heart and strength were exhausted. I obtained a degree, but I had been hesitating for nearly half a year, wandering on the crossroads. Don't you see that there are as many university students as crucian carp these days? Counting on my fingers, how many people have a proper occupation?

Art News: Mr. Zhi Fa is particularly skilled in the six methods of painting. He traveled with Anji from Shanyin, and his surviving works have been handed down, illuminating the ages. For the time being, he will succeed to the lineage of Wei Dan, expanding and flourishing his family's learning. His flowers followed Tianchi Fu Tang, his figures followed Xinluo, and his landscapes followed the Two Shi, and did not imitate the Four Wangs. He possessed all the strengths, a truly outstanding artist, comparable to Ren Wu. Rejoice! He will be holding a personal exhibition at the New Kaihe Flour Exchange on December 2nd, featuring over a hundred of his carefully refined works.

On the occasion of our sixtieth anniversary, in order to cater to the buying public in the local business community, we have established a circulating library and published a weekly amateur magazine. Now we feel the complexity of the local social environment, especially for the clerks and apprentices in various shops and branches, who have more opportunities to come into contact with society because of their work. In this situation, whether socially or individually, many difficult problems are bound to arise. However, individual wisdom is limited, and it is necessary to gather ideas and benefit each other in order to achieve mutual improvement. Therefore, we have specially added a "Clerk Correspondence" column to welcome everyone to raise various difficult questions. We are willing to do our best to discuss them with you sincerely, hoping to find a relatively appropriate and satisfactory solution. If there are topics that are beyond our intellectual ability to answer, we will ask experts to explain them separately.

Origin and Guidelines for Clerk Correspondence

Clerk Correspondence Guidelines

(1) Purpose of Correspondence: This column aims to gather ideas, explain difficult questions, mutually improve, and enhance the happiness of life.

(2) Target Audience: The target audience of this column is limited to clerks and apprentices in this area.

(3) Content of Correspondence: All questions concerning personal daily life, such as:

(i) Occupation (ii) Moral and intellectual cultivation (iii) Recreation and exercise (iv) Marriage, etc., as well as other questions relating to the state and society, are welcome. If the content of a question is too profound and beyond the capacity of this column, it can also be referred to the "Reader Advisor" of this newspaper for an answer.

(4) Method of Submission

(i) The letter must clearly state the name, age, place of origin, occupation, and detailed mailing address at the end; this information must be included in subsequent letters.

(ii) The writing style of the letter is not limited, but it should be simple, clear, and easy to understand, and it must be written clearly.

(iii) Please write "Shen Bao Local Supplement Clerk Correspondence Column Received" on the envelope; if a reply is required, please include a 2-cent postage stamp.

(iv) Correspondents must cut out the special stamp published in this column and paste it in the upper left corner of the letter; letters without the stamp will not be answered.

(5) Handling of Received Letters

(i) All questions discussed that the newspaper believes have public value may be disclosed in the newspaper.

(ii) To respect the opinions of correspondents, if a letter states that the sender does not wish to have their name disclosed, or if a separate reply is required, this can also be done.

(iii) If a correspondent wishes to have their letter disclosed in the newspaper, but the length of the letter is too long to disclose the full text, a summary will be published. If the content of a question is complex and requires careful research, resulting in a delayed answer or disclosure, readers are requested to understand. (iv) If there is a large number of letters, they will be answered in the order in which they are received; any delays are requested to be excused.

Novel

Sympathizer (Continued Part 2)

— Zhang Henshui

(On the threshing ground)

In front of Wang Lao Er's (Wang the Second) gate, there was a threshing ground. The ground was leveled and smoothed by stone rollers, so that any stray grains could be easily swept up during threshing. In front of the threshing ground, there was a row of trees. Beyond that was a clear pond. At night, the cool breeze blew from the water, making this an excellent place to cool off. So, after sunset, after eating dinner, Wang Lao San (Wang the Third) would carry a bucket of hot water and a bath basin to bathe under a short tree by the pond. After bathing, he would change into a pair of old and tattered pants, put on a pair of shoes that were only half intact, and then move a bamboo bed to rest in the breeze. His discarded pants and leftover water would be taken care of by the person who tended the stove. This night, there was a large moon, illuminating the threshing ground like a thin layer of snow. Wang Lao Er's wife was carrying a water bucket and bath basin, passing through the threshing ground and heading towards the gate, when Meng Guobao happened to walk by and called out, "Lao Er!" Wang Lao Er heard Meng's voice. He jumped up from the bamboo bed and said, "Oh! Mr. Meng, please sit down, please sit down. It's rare to have such a distinguished guest." Meng Guobao said, "What distinguished guest? My house and your house aren't even a hundred steps apart." Wang Lao Er fanned the bamboo bed with his banana leaf fan and said with a smile, "Please sit down, please sit down." Meng Guobao said, "I won't stand on ceremony," and sat down on the bamboo bed. Wang Lao Er then said to his wife, "Hurry and boil water for tea and stir-fry a plate of pumpkin seeds." His wife responded loudly with an "Oh!" Wang Lao Er was very polite. He was afraid that sitting together on a bamboo bed would be a bit unsuitable in the hot weather, so he sat on a stone roller opposite the bamboo bed. Meng Guobao said with a smile, "Lao Er, I just saw your sister-in-law carrying a bath basin and bucket inside. From the looks of it, she's not just tending the stove, but also doing chores for you. Isn't calling her the stove tender an incomplete description?" Wang Lao Er laughed and said, "How is it that Mr. Meng still remembers what I said during the day?" Meng Guobao smiled and said, "Because you and your sister-in-law don't call her anything when you talk to her. You just say your words louder, and she understands. Chinese people are really strange. Husbands and wives don't call each other by name. At most, they just say 'Hey.' The closest relationship should be with one's wife, but brothers, sisters, brothers-in-law, sisters-in-law, everyone in the family can be called something. Why is it that when it comes to husband and wife, they can't be addressed? Because of this, I thought of what you said during the day." Wang Lao Er laughed heartily and said, "That's a joke. Surely, I wouldn't call her 'stove tender this' and 'stove tender that,' would I?" As he said this, his new daughter-in-law carried a square stool out from the gate. Hearing this, she scolded softly, "You're talking nonsense again!" It seemed she was very averse to the term "stove tender." After saying these four words, she quietly placed the square stool in front of the bamboo bed and then brought a pottery teapot and two pairs of rice bowls. Wang Lao Er stood up and poured two bowls of tea, saying with a smile, "The bowls aren't good, but this tea is some Kill Two Tips tea that I brought from the mountains. You probably can't buy it in the city." Meng Guobao picked up the bowl and took a sip. Although the tea had a bit of a fragrant aroma, the bowl had a bit of rapeseed oil taste. Without saying a word, he put it down. Wang Lao Er held the bowl in both hands, like a monkey holding a peach, drinking it with great relish. His daughter-in-law came out again, still without saying a word, and placed a plate of freshly stir-fried pumpkin seeds on the square stool. Meng Guobao saw that she seemed afraid of people but not quite. Country women had a different kind of charm. In the moonlight, he saw that she had changed into a coarse summer cloth jacket, with her sleeves rolled up high. Under the hair on her ears, there were three or four jasmine flowers, which the country people called bathing flowers. Seeing that there were no wrinkles on her clothes, it seemed that she had also taken a bath and changed into fresh clothes. After she put down the pumpkin seeds, she didn't go back into the gate. Taking the palm-leaf fan in her hand, she fanned the dust off the stone steps and sat down on the steps. (To be continued)

Brief History of a Star

Anecdotes About Frank Buck, Author of "Bring 'Em Back Alive"

— Han

Anyone who has seen "Bring 'Em Back Alive" at the Nanjing Grand Theatre can feel how easily Frank Buck captured tigers, leopards, snakes, and other poisonous insects and wild beasts. Some may find it strange. But according to Frank himself, catching wild beasts is very simple. There is nothing strange about it. First, you only need to understand the temperament of the wild beasts, and second, you must have the courage and physical strength to adapt to the situation. Frank undoubtedly looks like a rough man. He can be extremely calm in dangerous situations, but cultural products such as telephones and underground railways make him feel uneasy. Once, on a ship, an orangutan escaped from its cage and approached him. At the critical moment, Frank punched the orangutan in the jaw and knocked it down. At that time, not only could he not get a gun, but he didn't even have time to turn around. So Frank is indeed a mentally and physically agile person.

Where did Frank get this strength and skill? It was probably inherited from his father. His father was originally a hunter. Even at the age of eighty-four, he still went fishing every day. When Frank was eight years old, he made a living by catching rattlesnakes. He caught these poisonous snakes and sold them to traveling medicine peddlers for five cents each. These traveling doctors bought them to make medicine, which was said to cure rheumatism. This is exactly in line with what is seen in southern Chinese society.

When Frank was seventeen, he "cherished great ambitions" to catch wild beasts. He secretly ran away from home and went to Chicago first. There was a small restaurant there, and he worked as a waiter. He worked hard. After accumulating some money, he went to South America. In South America, he made a living by catching birds. He caught the birds and sold them in the United States. In this way, his hunting career became more and more prosperous day by day. Later, he was even able to set up an agency in Singapore in the East. This was the beginning of his hunting for wild beasts in the forests around Singapore.

Frank's life is very profitable. Some birds can sell for a thousand gold dollars each. An elephant can sell for more than two thousand five hundred gold dollars. Circuses, zoos, and various private gardens are all his sales venues. He is from Texas, so most of the wild beasts in the zoos in the cities of Texas are supplied by Frank. It is said that there are as many as seventy-two kinds of rare birds and animals.

According to Frank himself, he waited three weeks before the fight between the python and the tiger, because he found that the python had just swallowed a wild boar. The wild boar would take at least eleven days to digest in the python's stomach, so it would not go out to look for food until it was hungry again, and only then could it fight with the tiger. But the python and the tiger fought so much, but neither was seriously injured, and both were able to "retreat with their whole army," which is a bit strange. But to say it's fake, it's so lifelike.

Frank is now forty-two years old, six feet tall, and has a very rough appearance, but he has a very beautiful wife. It is said that they have never argued since they got married. This wife is his second wife. Because Frank had already married a woman who was ten years older than him when he was nineteen. But later, that woman felt uneasy about being an older wife to a younger husband, so she retreated to the ranks of friends. So Frank remarried this young and beautiful woman. They also have a daughter, who is now eight months old.

Currently, Cathay is showing a historical secret from twenty years ago, "Five Star Final," starring Edward G. Robinson.

Local News

Wang Fuqing is Going Abroad

— Qingxia

Wang Fuqing has been in the film industry for more than ten years. He founded the Great East Golden Lion Company himself. His first production, "Spring Breeze and Willows," is about to be completed, with only a few outdoor scenes remaining to be filmed. A few days ago, he specially sent someone to Xia Peizhen's home, asking Xia to come to Great East in three days, and then go to Suzhou together to shoot outdoor scenes, because he hoped that this "Spring Breeze and Willows" would be completed in the shortest possible time.

But he is not just rushing to complete this "Spring Breeze and Willows," it is really because after he finishes "Spring Breeze and Willows," he wants to go to the United States to investigate on the ground. As for all the affairs of the company, he said his cousin Shen Zhiyuan can act as his agent.

We said in the article, we sincerely hope that Mr. Wang will work hard for the film industry with 120 points of sincerity. He should be single-minded and persevering to cultivate this precarious domestic film industry. He goes abroad this time, and when he returns home one day, the second production of Great East may make a surprising contribution.

Opinion After Opinion

Those Engaged in Art Should Accept the Opinions of the Audience

— Yi Lie

Since the creation of this magazine, in a short month, many loyal readers have expressed their opinions every day. Whether the film companies, directors, actors, and the authorities of various theaters have accepted and implemented the fair criticisms, sincere suggestions, and honest warnings of the audience—that is, the readers of this magazine—is a matter of concern and knowledge for those who love movies.

The opinions published by all the companies in this magazine are the sincere expressions of those who love movies, and they are all based on facts and theories. Will the film companies, directors, actors, and theaters adopt them? Or will they treat them like wind in their ears? The audience has no right to interfere, but I think that those engaged in film art will not be so stubborn and go their own way.

"Lianhua Weekly" is Published Today

— Xing

The film magazine, which has been suspended for a year, was originally published by Lianhua Company. Recently, there was news of its revival, which this magazine reported earlier. It is now known that the magazine has not been revived, but the preparers of Lianhua are actually the reincarnation of the magazine, named "Lianhua Weekly." The magazine is edited by playwright Wang Shaoqing. The inaugural issue is scheduled to be published today, and various theaters will have it for sale.
